# Progress Log

## 2026-02-27 ŌĆö Task 0.1.4: Add required dependencies
**What was done:**
- Added `@alloy-js/csharp` (0.22.0) to `dependencies` ŌĆö needed for C# code generation components (ClassDeclaration, Property, Method, etc.)
- Added `@typespec/http` (^1.9.0) and `@typespec/rest` (>=0.79.0 <0.80.0) to `peerDependencies` ŌĆö TypeSpec HTTP libraries provided by the user's project
- Added `@azure-tools/typespec-client-generator-core` (>=0.65.3 <0.66.0) to `peerDependencies` ŌĆö TCGC for SDK client model
- Added matching dev versions of all new peer deps for testing
- Changed `@typespec/compiler` peer dep from exact `"1.9.0"` to `"^1.9.0"` to match legacy emitter pattern
- Fixed `vitest.config.ts` to scope test discovery to `test/` only (was running 920 submodule test files)

**Pattern used:** Followed the legacy emitter pattern ŌĆö TypeSpec ecosystem packages as peerDependencies, Alloy packages as direct dependencies.

**Important for next iterations:**
- All packages were already installed in node_modules (via autoInstallPeers or transitive deps) ŌĆö adding them to package.json just makes them explicit
- The vitest config now includes `test: { include: ["test/**/*.test.{ts,tsx}"] }` ŌĆö always scope test discovery to avoid submodule tests
- `@alloy-js/typescript` is kept even though this is a C# emitter because `@typespec/emitter-framework` requires it as a peer dependency

## 2026-02-27 ŌĆö Task 0.3.1: Create root HttpClientCSharpOutput component
**What was done:**
- Created `src/components/HttpClientCSharpOutput.tsx` ŌĆö root output component that wraps emitter-framework's `Output` with C# name policy and format options
- Updated `src/emitter.tsx` ŌĆö replaced ExampleComponent/SourceFile scaffolding with HttpClientCSharpOutput
- Exported component from `src/components/index.ts` barrel file
- Updated `test/hello.test.ts` ŌĆö new tests verify emitter compiles without diagnostics and empty output produces no files

**Design decision:**
- HttpClientCSharpOutput wraps Output (self-contained) rather than being content inside Output. This keeps all C# configuration in one place and makes emitter.tsx thin.
- Output from `@typespec/emitter-framework` (not `@alloy-js/core`) ŌĆö provides TspContext so child components can use `useTsp()`

**Key patterns:**
- `createCSharpNamePolicy()` from `@alloy-js/csharp` ŌĆö handles PascalCase for types, camelCase for params
- Format options: tabWidth=4, printWidth=120 (matches CSharpFormatOptions defaults)
- Component accepts `children` prop for future content (models, enums, clients)

**Notes for next iterations:**
- ExampleComponent.tsx left in place (not deleted) ŌĆö can be cleaned up later
- ESLint config is broken (missing @eslint/js) ŌĆö pre-existing, not our issue
- Prettier has submodule plugin error ŌĆö pre-existing, not our issue

## 2026-02-27 ŌĆö Task 0.1.1: Define emitter options interface
**What was done:**
- Created `src/options.ts` with:
  - `LicenseOptions` interface (sub-interface for license configuration)
  - `CSharpEmitterOptions` interface ŌĆö all user-facing emitter options
  - `CSharpEmitterOptionsSchema` ŌĆö JSON Schema for TypeSpec compiler config validation
  - `defaultOptions` ŌĆö default values matching legacy emitter behavior
  - `resolveOptions()` ŌĆö merges user options with defaults
- Created `test/options.test.ts` with 12 tests covering interface shape, schema validation, defaults, and option resolution

**Design decision:**
- Included interface + schema + defaults + resolver in one file, matching legacy pattern (`submodules/typespec/packages/http-client-csharp/emitter/src/options.ts`)
- Excluded C#-generator-specific options: debug, generator-name, emitter-extension-path, update-code-model, sdk-context-options, logLevel (not needed in single-phase emitter)
- Included: api-version, generate-protocol-methods, generate-convenience-methods, unreferenced-types-handling, new-project, save-inputs, disable-xml-docs, package-name, license

**Notes for next iterations:**
- Task 0.1.2 (Register emitter options in library) can use `CSharpEmitterOptionsSchema` directly from this file
- Task 0.3.2 (EmitterContext provider) will consume `resolveOptions()` from this file
- `defaultOptions` uses `Required<Pick<...>>` to type only the fields that have defaults ŌĆö other fields remain optional

## 2026-02-27 ŌĆö Task 0.1.3: Implement $onEmit entry point
- Rewrote `src/emitter.tsx` with full $onEmit implementation:
  - Typed `EmitContext<CSharpEmitterOptions>` for type-safe options access
  - Added `noEmit` guard to skip emission when `--no-emit` is passed
  - Calls `resolveOptions(context)` to merge user options with defaults
  - Calls `createSdkContext(context, $lib.name)` to create TCGC SdkContext
  - Reports TCGC diagnostics to the TypeSpec program
  - Passes `options` and `sdkContext` as props to `HttpClientCSharpOutput`
- Updated `HttpClientCSharpOutput` to accept `options` (ResolvedCSharpEmitterOptions) and `sdkContext` (SdkContext) props
- Added `ResolvedCSharpEmitterOptions` type alias in `src/options.ts` with explicit return type on `resolveOptions()`
- Exported `ApiTester` from `test/test-host.ts` for tests needing custom emitter options
- Created `test/emitter.test.ts` with 4 tests: service compilation, model processing, no-output verification, custom options

**Key pattern:** createSdkContext is called in $onEmit (not in components) because it's async. The SdkContext is passed as a prop to HttpClientCSharpOutput; task 0.3.2 will wrap it in an EmitterContext provider for deep access via useEmitterContext().

**Gotcha:** `Tester.compileAndDiagnose()` only accepts `TestCompileOptions` (with `compilerOptions`), NOT emitter options. To test with custom emitter options, create a separate tester via `ApiTester.emit("http-client-csharp", { ...options })`.

## 2026-02-27 ŌĆö Task 0.2.1: Create System.ClientModel core builtins

**Summary:** Created Alloy library declarations for System.ClientModel types using `createLibrary()` from `@alloy-js/csharp`. Two libraries declared:

1. `SystemClientModel` ("System.ClientModel") ŌĆö ClientResult (with FromValue, FromResponse), BinaryContent (with Create)
2. `SystemClientModelPrimitives` ("System.ClientModel.Primitives") ŌĆö ClientPipeline (Create, CreateMessage, Send, SendAsync), PipelineMessage (Request, Response, BufferResponse, ExtractResponse, Apply), PipelineRequest (Headers, Content, Uri), PipelineResponse (Status, Content, ContentStream, Headers, IsError), PipelinePolicy, PipelineMessageClassifier (Create)

**Files created:**
- `src/builtins/system-client-model.ts` ŌĆö Library declarations with JSDoc on every type and member
- `src/builtins/index.ts` ŌĆö Re-exports
- `test/builtins.test.tsx` ŌĆö 11 tests: structural checks + using statement generation via render()

**Key patterns:**
- Two separate `createLibrary()` calls for the two namespaces ŌĆö future tasks (0.2.2ŌĆō0.2.6) will add types to the same file
- Cross-library type references use arrow functions for lazy evaluation (e.g., PipelineMessage.Request ŌåÆ PipelineRequest, PipelineRequest.Content ŌåÆ BinaryContent)
- Using statement test uses `render(<Output><SourceFile>...</SourceFile></Output>)` from `@alloy-js/core` with C# `SourceFile`, `ClassDeclaration`, and `Property` to verify correct `using` directives
- Members without cross-library type refs intentionally omit `type` (consistent with alloy builtins pattern)

**Design decision:** Two separate `createLibrary` calls (one per namespace) rather than a nested namespace descriptor. This matches the alloy builtins convention and allows independent imports.

## 2026-02-27 ŌĆö Task 0.3.4: Implement license header rendering
**What was done:**
- Created `src/utils/header.ts` with `getLicenseHeader(options)` function
- The function generates the standard C# file header matching the legacy emitter's golden file format
- Supports three modes: (1) raw `header` string with `// ` prefix per line, (2) constructed from `company` + `name` fields, (3) minimal header with no license info
- Always includes `// <auto-generated/>` marker and `#nullable disable` directive
- Created `test/header.test.ts` with 9 tests covering all configurations and edge cases

**Design decisions:**
- Utility function approach (not a JSX component) since header is static text that works directly as SourceFile's `header` prop Children
- Raw `header` field lines get `// ` prefix (matches legacy CodeWriter.ToString behavior)
- When no raw header is provided, constructs from `company` and `name` fields
- When no license config at all, emits only auto-generated marker and nullable disable

**Patterns used:**
- Returns a `\n`-joined string compatible with Alloy SourceFile `header` prop
- Downstream usage: `<SourceFile header={getLicenseHeader(options)}>...</SourceFile>`

**For next iterations:**
- This unblocks 1.4.1 (FixedEnumFile), 1.6.1 (ExtensibleEnumFile), and 1.2.1 (ModelFile, which also needs 1.1.2)
- The `header` prop on Alloy SourceFile renders content before `using` directives with an automatic blank line separator
- Do NOT use `<Prose>` for the header ŌĆö it collapses whitespace and word-wraps, destroying the exact format

## 2026-02-28 ŌĆö Task 1.4.1: Create FixedEnumFile component
**What was done:**
- Created `src/components/enums/FixedEnumFile.tsx` ŌĆö generates C# enum files from TCGC SdkEnumType
- Component uses @alloy-js/csharp EnumDeclaration + EnumMember directly (not emitter-framework wrapper)
- Doc comments use TCGC `summary` ŌåÆ `doc` ŌåÆ `{name}.` fallback chain matching legacy DocHelpers
- Header rendered as raw text children in C# SourceFile (SourceFile lacks `header` prop)
- Wired into emitter.tsx: filters `sdkContext.sdkPackage.enums` by `isFixed` and renders FixedEnumFile for each
- Created `src/components/enums/index.ts` barrel export
- Updated `src/components/index.ts` to export FixedEnumFile
- Added `HttpTester` to `test/test-host.ts` with `.importLibraries()` for HTTP decorator support
- Created `test/fixed-enum.test.ts` with 7 tests covering: enum generation, header, doc comments, namespace, no values for string-backed, no output when empty, @doc decorator

**Design decisions:**
- Used @alloy-js/csharp EnumDeclaration directly instead of emitter-framework wrapper because:
  1. Need control over doc comment generation (TCGC fallback to member name)
  2. Need future extensibility for int-backed enum values (EnumMember lacks value prop)
  3. TCGC types are our primary data source, not TypeSpec types
- Single-line doc comment format `/// <summary> ... </summary>` via raw strings (matching golden file)
- Header as children (not prop) because @alloy-js/csharp SourceFile doesn't expose a `header` prop

**Patterns used:**
- `useCSharpNamePolicy()` for enum and member naming
- `refkey(sdkType)` with TCGC objects as seeds for stable cross-file references
- `<For each={...} joiner={",\n"}>` for comma-separated enum members
- `HttpTester = Tester.importLibraries()` to enable `using TypeSpec.Http;` in tests

**Known issues:**
- Namespace brace style is K&R (`namespace N {`) instead of Allman (`namespace N\n{`). This is an Alloy Block formatting default ŌĆö not controllable at component level.
- @alloy-js/csharp SourceFile doesn't have a `header` prop. Header is injected as raw text children before Namespace.

- String-backed and float-backed enums remain without initialization values (C# can't hold string/float constants)
- Added 3 new tests: int-backed enum values, float-backed enum no-values, non-sequential int values (flag-style)

**Design decisions:**
- Append value text as sibling after EnumMember in JSX fragment (e.g., `<EnumMember .../>{" = 1"}`) rather than using `code` template tag ŌĆö simpler and preserves refkey tracking
- Used `isSdkIntKind` from TCGC rather than manual kind string checks ŌĆö future-proof against new int types

**Patterns used:**
- `isSdkIntKind(sdkEnum.valueType.kind)` to classify backing type
- TypeSpec integer enum syntax: `enum Priority { Low: 0, High: 1 }` for int-backed
- TypeSpec float enum syntax: `enum Temp { Cold: 32.5 }` for float-backed

**Test coverage:**
- 10 total tests in fixed-enum.test.ts (7 existing + 3 new)
- All 64 tests pass across 7 test files

## 2026-02-28 ŌĆö Task 1.5.1: Create FixedEnumSerializationFile component

**Summary:** Created `src/components/enums/FixedEnumSerializationFile.tsx` that generates `{EnumName}.Serialization.cs` files with serialization extension methods for fixed enums. The component produces an `internal static partial class {EnumName}Extensions` containing:

- **ToSerial{TypeName}** (switch expression): Converts enum ŌåÆ underlying value. Skipped for int-backed enums.
- **To{EnumName}** (if-chain): Converts underlying value ŌåÆ enum. Uses `StringComparer.OrdinalIgnoreCase.Equals()` for strings, `==` for numerics.

**Files created/modified:**
- `src/components/enums/FixedEnumSerializationFile.tsx` ŌĆö main component with SerializeMethod and DeserializeMethod sub-components
- `src/components/enums/index.ts` ŌĆö barrel export
- `src/components/index.ts` ŌĆö barrel export
- `src/emitter.tsx` ŌĆö wired serialization file alongside FixedEnumFile
- `test/fixed-enum-serialization.test.ts` ŌĆö 7 tests covering string/int/float-backed enums

**Patterns used:**
- Renders method bodies as individual string children separated by `{"\n"}`, matching FixedEnumFile's line-by-line approach
- Uses leading spaces in string literals for internal indentation (e.g., `"    if (...)"` for 4-space indent within method body)
- Helper functions: `getCSharpTypeInfo()` maps TCGC kinds to C# keywords/framework names, `formatValueLiteral()` formats values with type-appropriate suffixes

**Key observations:**
- Alloy's rendering engine indents each string child to the current context level; embedded `\n` resets to that level
- `using System;` rendered as raw text (not via SourceFile auto-using) since we use raw type names for System types
- ParameterProps in @alloy-js/csharp lacks `this` modifier, so extension methods are rendered as raw strings

**Test count: 71 total (7 new), all passing.**

2026-02-28 ŌĆö Task 1.1.2: Add missing type mappings (complete)

Created CSharpScalarOverrides provider component that overrides emitter-framework's TypeExpression scalar mappings to match the legacy HTTP client C# emitter.

Key deliverables:
- Created `src/components/CSharpTypeExpression.tsx` with:
  - SystemBinaryData library declaration (BinaryData not in alloy builtins)
  - scalarOverrideMap with 7 scalar overrides
  - getScalarOverride() function that correctly distinguishes built-in vs user-defined scalars
  - CSharpScalarOverrides provider using Experimental_ComponentOverrides
  - Intrinsic override for unknown ŌåÆ BinaryData
- Created `test/type-expression.test.tsx` with 20 tests covering all overrides and fall-throughs
- Integrated CSharpScalarOverrides into emitter.tsx (wraps component tree)
- All 139 tests pass; build succeeds

Design decision: Used Experimental_ComponentOverrides (forTypeKind) instead of a standalone wrapper component. This automatically applies to all <TypeExpression> usages in the subtree including framework-internal ones. Follows the flight-instructor pattern.

Key gotcha: The getScalarOverride function must use intrinsicNameToCSharpType from the emitter-framework to distinguish built-in scalars from user-defined ones. Without this, walking the base chain causes int32 (extends integer) to incorrectly pick up the integerŌåÆlong override. Built-in scalars check only their direct name; user-defined scalars walk the chain.

Stream/IPAddress note: These are NOT TypeSpec scalars or SdkBuiltInKinds. They were legacy InputPrimitiveType values. In the new TCGC, they're handled at a different layer (model/property level).

Overrides: bytesŌåÆBinaryData, integerŌåÆlong, safeintŌåÆlong, numericŌåÆdouble, floatŌåÆdouble, plainDateŌåÆDateTimeOffset, plainTimeŌåÆTimeSpan, unknownŌåÆBinaryData

Next tasks: 1.1.3 (collection type utilities), 1.1.4 (nullable type utilities), or other ready phase-0/1 tasks

2026-02-28 ŌĆö Task 1.1.4: Create nullable type utilities (complete)

Created nullable type utilities for C# code generation in src/utils/nullable.ts.

- **Key deliverables:**
  - `isPropertyNullable(property)` ŌĆö determines if a property should render as T? in C#
  - `unwrapNullableType(type)` ŌĆö strips SdkNullableType wrapper for TypeExpression
  - `isCollectionType(type)` ŌĆö checks array/dict (collections are never nullable)
  - 26 unit tests in test/nullable.test.ts covering all type categories

- **Design decision:** Three separate functions (not a single combined resolver) for composability. The property nullable check accepts any `{ type: SdkType; optional: boolean }` shape, not just SdkModelPropertyType, for flexibility across property-like contexts.

- **Rules implemented (matching legacy PropertyProvider.cs lines 86-88):**
  - Optional non-collection types ŌåÆ nullable (both value and reference types, matching legacy)
  - Required types ŌåÆ not nullable
  - Collections (array/dict) ŌåÆ never nullable, even when wrapped in SdkNullableType
  - Explicitly nullable types (SdkNullableType wrapper) ŌåÆ nullable (unless collection)

- **TCGC insight:** SdkNullableType is TCGC's representation of `T | null`. It wraps the inner type. The `optional` flag on properties is orthogonal ŌĆö a property can be optional without SdkNullableType, or have SdkNullableType without being optional.

- **Usage pattern for downstream tasks (1.2.2 model properties):**
  ```tsx
  const innerType = unwrapNullableType(prop.type);
  const nullable = isPropertyNullable(prop);
  <Property type={<TypeExpression type={innerType} />} nullable={nullable} />
  ```

- **Next tasks ready:** 1.2.2 (model property generation ŌĆö now unblocked), 1.1.5 (type mapping tests ŌĆö needs 1.1.3 too)

2026-02-28 ŌĆö Task 1.2.2: Implement model property generation (complete)

Created `src/components/models/ModelProperty.tsx` with:
- `propertyHasSetter(modelUsage)` ŌĆö determines setter presence based on UsageFlags bitmap
  - Input-only models: get-only (constructor handles initialization)
  - Output-only models: get-only (deserialization populates)
  - Input+Output models: get+set (user sets for requests, server populates for responses)
- `ModelProperty` component ŌĆö renders C# auto-property using Alloy Property component
  - Uses TypeExpression with `type.__raw!` to convert TCGC SdkType ŌåÆ TypeSpec Type
  - Nullable via `isPropertyNullable()` from nullable utils
  - XML doc comments in `/// <summary> text </summary>` format matching legacy emitter
  - PascalCase naming via Alloy's built-in naming policy

Modified `src/components/models/ModelFile.tsx`:
- Added `<For>` loop with `hardline` joiner over model properties
- Each property rendered via `<ModelProperty>` inside ClassDeclaration body

Key design decision: Used Alloy's Property component with auto-property syntax (`{ get; }` / `{ get; set; }`)
instead of the legacy emitter's `=> throw null` pattern. Auto-properties are functionally correct and
the serialization partial class (Phase 2) can work with the backing fields.

Important discovery: TypeExpression from @typespec/emitter-framework/csharp expects TypeSpec compiler `Type`,
NOT TCGC `SdkType`. Use `sdkType.__raw!` to access the raw TypeSpec Type. This works for all types where
TCGC preserves the raw reference (scalars, models, enums). Synthetic types may need different handling.

10 new tests added covering: get/set accessors, get-only for input/output models, nullable types,
doc comments, PascalCase naming, scalar type mapping, and property spacing.

Unblocks: 1.2.3 (required vs optional logic), 1.2.6 (additionalBinaryDataProperties), 1.2.7 (XML doc comments)

2026-02-28 ŌĆö Task 1.2.3: Implement required vs optional property logic (complete)

Created `src/utils/property.ts` with required/optional property analysis utilities:
- `isCSharpReferenceType(type)` ŌĆö determines if TCGC type maps to C# reference type (for null validation)
- `isPropertyReadOnly(property)` ŌĆö checks if visibility is [Read] only
- `isConstructorParameter(property, isStruct?)` ŌĆö whether property is a public constructor param
- `propertyRequiresNullCheck(property)` ŌĆö whether property needs Argument.AssertNotNull
- `getPropertyInitializerKind(property)` ŌĆö returns initialization kind (change-tracking-list/dict, to-list/dict, direct-assign, none)

Updated `propertyHasSetter` in ModelProperty.tsx:
- Now accepts property object (not just usage flags) for more nuanced logic
- Collections never have setters (mutation via collection interface)
- Read-only properties (visibility=[Read]) never have setters
- Optional properties on input-only models DO get setters (object initializer syntax)
- Required properties on input-only models remain get-only (constructor handles init)

Key design decision: Pure utility functions (no JSX) for property analysis. Easier to test in isolation and downstream constructor tasks (1.2.4, 1.2.5) can import these.

Tests: 35 new tests (20 model integration + 35 property-utils unit) covering all new utility functions and updated property behavior. Total: 217 tests passing.

2026-02-28 ŌĆö Task 1.2.5: Implement internal serialization constructor (complete)

Added the internal serialization constructor to `ModelConstructors.tsx`:
- Always `internal` access modifier (regardless of model usage)
- Parameters: ALL model properties (including optional and read-only) + `additionalBinaryDataProperties` as last param (type: `IDictionary<string, BinaryData>`)
- Body: Direct property assignment for ALL properties, no `Argument.AssertNotNull` validation
- Assigns `_additionalBinaryDataProperties = additionalBinaryDataProperties;` for round-trip serialization fidelity

Key technical challenge: Alloy's `<Constructor>` component deduplicates names when two constructors exist in the same class, appending `_2` to the second constructor name. Created `OverloadConstructor` component that sets `ignoreNameConflict: true` on the MethodSymbol, enabling valid C# constructor overloading.

New exports from ModelConstructors.tsx:
- `ADDITIONAL_BINARY_DATA_PROPS_FIELD_NAME` (`_additionalBinaryDataProperties`)
- `ADDITIONAL_BINARY_DATA_PROPS_PARAM_NAME` (`additionalBinaryDataProperties`)

Added 8 new tests for the serialization constructor. Updated 2 existing tests that assumed only one constructor exists (scoped their assertions to the public constructor specifically).

Pattern: `OverloadConstructor` should be used for any additional constructor overload in the same class to avoid Alloy symbol deduplication.

## 2026-02-28 ŌĆö Task 1.3.4: Implement Unknown discriminator variant (complete)

**What was done:**
- Created `src/components/models/UnknownDiscriminatorModel.tsx` ŌĆö new component that generates `Unknown{BaseName}.cs` for each abstract discriminated base model
- Modified `src/components/models/ModelConstructors.tsx` ŌĆö exported `OverloadConstructor`, `buildSerializationParameters`, and `ModelConstructorProps` for reuse
- Modified `src/emitter.tsx` ŌĆö added rendering of `UnknownDiscriminatorModelFile` for models matching `isModelAbstract()`
- Added 6 new tests (252 total passing)

**Pattern details:**
- Unknown variant is `internal partial class Unknown{BaseName} : {BaseName}`
- Single internal constructor with base model's serialization params (all props + additionalBinaryDataProperties)
- String discriminator null-guard: `kind ?? "unknown"`
- Enum discriminator default-check: `kind != default ? kind : "unknown"` (works via extensible enum implicit string conversion)
- Constructor body is empty (all initialization done by base ctor)
- Unknown variant is NOT in TCGC model ŌĆö it's synthesized by the emitter for each abstract discriminated base

**Key decisions:**
- Reused `OverloadConstructor` from ModelConstructors.tsx instead of creating a new component (simpler, works fine even with single constructor)
- Used `buildSerializationParameters` for constructor params (exact same signature as base model's serialization ctor)
- `isModelAbstract()` (already exported) used in emitter.tsx to filter which models get Unknown variants

**Notes for future tasks:**
- Task 1.3.5 (additional properties on derived models): may need to handle Unknown variants with additional properties
- Task 1.3.6 (multi-level discriminator chains): Unknown variant for mid-level base models would need params from the full inheritance chain (recursive collection of serialization params)
- Task 2.4.3 (Unknown fallback deserialization): will need a `DeserializeUnknown{Name}` method that creates the Unknown variant instance

2026-02-28 ŌĆö Task 1.3.5: Already implemented (marked done)

Verified that derived model additional properties (task 1.3.5) was already fully implemented and tested. All three acceptance criteria met: own properties rendered, constructor includes both base and derived params, base call includes base params only. Marked as done.

2026-02-28 ŌĆö Task 1.3.6: Handle multi-level discriminator chains (complete)

Fixed 5 interconnected bugs affecting nested discriminator hierarchies (e.g., Fish ŌåÆ Shark ŌåÆ SawShark):

1. **isModelAbstract bug**: Added `model.discriminatorValue === undefined` check. Without this, intermediate models like Shark (which have BOTH discriminated subtypes AND a discriminator value) were incorrectly marked abstract.

2. **Discriminator property filtering**: Replaced `!p.discriminator` with `!isBaseDiscriminatorOverride(p)`. The new function only filters out constant/enumvalue discriminator overrides (like `kind: "shark"`), keeping the model's own discriminator property (like `sharktype: string`).

3. **Hierarchy-walking for ctor params**: Added `collectBaseNonDiscCtorParams()` and `computePublicCtorParams()` which walk the full inheritance chain recursively. This ensures 3rd-level models (SawShark) get grandparent params (age from Fish).

4. **Base call parameter ordering**: Replaced fixed "discriminator-first" approach with `buildPublicBaseInitializer()` that matches the base model's ctor param order. Critical for Shark's ctor `(int age, string sharktype)` where discriminator isn't first.

5. **Serialization param ordering**: Added `computeSerializationCtorParams()` which recursively builds serialization ctor params, correctly positioning `additionalBinaryDataProperties` between base and own params.

Also added `hasDiscriminatedSubtypes()` for Unknown variant generation (separate from abstract check), ensuring UnknownShark is generated for intermediate models.

8 new tests in the NestedDiscriminator describe block covering: intermediate model non-abstract, own discriminator property, hierarchy param collection, 3rd-level params, serialization param ordering, Unknown variant generation, and null-guards.

Key pattern: Always use `pnpm build` before `pnpm test` ŌĆö vitest resolves through dist/ not source.

2026-02-28 ŌĆö Task 2.1.1: Create ModelSerializationFile component (complete)

Created `src/components/serialization/ModelSerializationFile.tsx` ŌĆö generates `.Serialization.cs` partial class files implementing `IJsonModel<T>`.

**Key design decisions:**
- Uses `code` template with `SystemClientModelPrimitives.IJsonModel` builtin refkey for the interface type. This auto-generates `using System.ClientModel.Primitives;` via Alloy's SourceFile.
- Uses `namekey(modelName, { ignoreNameConflict: true })` from `@alloy-js/core` to prevent Alloy's symbol deduplication. Without this, the serialization file's ClassDeclaration would be renamed `Widget_2` because ModelFile already declares a ClassDeclaration with the same name in the same namespace.
- No refkey on the serialization ClassDeclaration ŌĆö the ModelFile already owns the type's refkey.
- Re-declares baseType for derived models (matching golden file pattern: `Dog : Pet, IJsonModel<Dog>`).
- Abstract models get the abstract modifier in the serialization file.
- Accepts `children` prop for future tasks to add serialization methods.

**Files created:**
- `src/components/serialization/ModelSerializationFile.tsx` ŌĆö component
- `src/components/serialization/index.ts` ŌĆö barrel export
- `test/model-serialization.test.ts` ŌĆö 8 tests covering path, header, interface, namespace, derived, abstract, hierarchy

**Files modified:**
- `src/emitter.tsx` ŌĆö renders serialization files for all models
- `docs/prd.json` ŌĆö marked 2.1.1 as done

**Known cosmetic differences from golden files:**
- Alloy's SourceFile places `using` directives before the license header. Golden files have header first. This is an Alloy framework behavior, not specific to the serialization file.
- Empty class body renders as `class Widget;` (semicolon) instead of `class Widget { }`. This is valid C# 12+ and will resolve when methods are added in later tasks.

**Learnings:**
- TCGC model `namespace` property does NOT include `.Models` suffix (e.g., `TestNamespace`, not `TestNamespace.Models`). Test expectations should match this.
- `namekey()` from `@alloy-js/core` with `{ ignoreNameConflict: true }` is the correct way to handle partial class declarations across files. Same pattern as `OverloadConstructor`.

Total tests: 276 (all passing). Build succeeds.

**Next natural tasks:** 2.1.2 (interface determination), 2.1.3 (parameterless internal constructor), 1.1.3 (collection type utilities), 1.2.6 (additionalBinaryDataProperties)

2026-02-28 ŌĆö Task 2.2.4: Implement DateTime serialization with encoding (complete)

Evolved `getWriteMethodName` ŌåÆ `getWriteMethodInfo` in `PropertySerializer.tsx`:

- Handles utcDateTime/offsetDateTime with encoding-based format specifiers:
  - rfc3339 ŌåÆ WriteStringValue(prop, "O")
  - rfc7231 ŌåÆ WriteStringValue(prop, "R")

- plainDate with "D" format

and Bytes (2.2.6) which also need format specifiers. Future tasks should add cases to

2026-02-28 ŌĆö Task 2.2.5: Implement Duration serialization (complete)

- Added `getDurationWriteInfo()` and `getDurationNumericWriteInfo()` to `PropertySerializer.tsx`
- Duration encoding ŌåÆ C# output mapping:
  - ISO8601 (default) ŌåÆ `writer.WriteStringValue(Prop, "P")`
  - seconds + float ŌåÆ `writer.WriteNumberValue(Prop.TotalSeconds)`
  - seconds + int ŌåÆ `writer.WriteNumberValue(Convert.ToInt32(Prop.TotalSeconds))`
  - milliseconds + float ŌåÆ `writer.WriteNumberValue(Prop.TotalMilliseconds)`
  - milliseconds + int ŌåÆ `writer.WriteNumberValue(Convert.ToInt32(Prop.TotalMilliseconds))`
- Extended `WriteMethodInfo` with optional `valueTransform` callback to handle value wrapping
  (e.g., `.TotalSeconds`, `Convert.ToInt32(...)`) ŌĆö this is reusable for bytes (2.2.6)
- Added `INTEGER_KINDS` set for wire type checking (integer vs float distinction)
- Updated `WritePropertySerialization` to use `valueTransform` when present
- Added 5 new tests covering all duration encoding variants
- All 313 tests pass
- Design decision: Chose `valueTransform` callback over separate handling in component
  for clean separation of type analysis vs rendering. Rejected string templates (less type-safe)
  and prefix/suffix pattern (awkward with nested parens).

2026-02-28 ŌĆö Task 2.2.11: Implement optional property guards (complete)

Modified `src/components/serialization/PropertySerializer.tsx` to wrap optional property writes in `Optional.IsDefined`/`Optional.IsCollectionDefined` guards:

- Added `needsOptionalGuard(property)` ŌĆö returns true for `property.optional` properties
- Added `getOptionalGuardMethodName(property)` ŌĆö returns "IsCollectionDefined" for collections, "IsDefined" for scalars
- Extracted `renderWriteStatements()` helper to handle indentation (4 spaces unguarded, 8 spaces inside guard block)
- Modified `WritePropertySerialization` to conditionally wrap write statements in `if (Optional.GuardMethod(Prop)) { ... }` block

Design decision: Guard logic lives inside `WritePropertySerialization` (not as a separate wrapper component) because the guard tightly couples to the serialization ŌĆö it wraps both WritePropertyName and WriteValue together. This keeps the code simple and means future type serialization tasks (2.2.6-2.2.10) will automatically get guards when they add support for their types.

Tests added (7 new tests in `OptionalPropertyGuards` describe block):
- Optional string ŌåÆ IsDefined guard
- Optional int32 ŌåÆ IsDefined guard
- Required non-nullable ŌåÆ no guard
- Indentation correctness inside guard block
- Optional boolean ŌåÆ IsDefined guard
- Mixed required/optional model ŌåÆ guards only on optional
- Optional utcDateTime ŌåÆ IsDefined guard with format specifier

Note for task 2.2.12: The required-nullable if/else pattern (with WriteNull fallback) is not yet implemented ŌĆö that's the next task. The guard infrastructure is ready for it.

2026-02-28 ŌĆö Task 2.2.12: Implement required-nullable write pattern (complete)

Modified `src/components/serialization/PropertySerializer.tsx` to handle required-nullable properties (properties with `type.kind === "nullable"` that are NOT optional).

Changes:
- Added `isRequiredNullable(property)` ŌĆö detects `!optional && !collection && type.kind === "nullable"`
- Added `needsNullableValueAccess(property)` ŌĆö checks if `.Value` is needed (nullable value types like int?, bool?, DateTimeOffset?)
- Expanded `needsOptionalGuard()` to return true for required-nullable properties (they also need Optional.IsDefined)
- Modified `WritePropertySerialization` to render an else branch with `writer.WriteNull("name"u8)` for required-nullable
- Added `.Value` accessor for nullable value types inside the guard block

Pattern generated for required-nullable value types (e.g., `int | null`):
```csharp
if (Optional.IsDefined(Count))
{
    writer.WritePropertyName("count"u8);
    writer.WriteNumberValue(Count.Value);
}
else
{
    writer.WriteNull("count"u8);
}
```

Reference types (string, url) don't get `.Value` but still get the else branch.

Tests added: 7 new tests in `RequiredNullableWritePattern` describe block covering:
- Required nullable string (reference type, no .Value)
- Required nullable int32 (value type, .Value)
- Required nullable boolean (value type, .Value)
- Required nullable utcDateTime (value type, .Value + format specifier)
- Indentation verification for if/else block
- Mixed required/optional/required-nullable model
- Required nullable URL (reference type, no .Value)

Known gap: Optional nullable value types (e.g., `count?: int32` ŌåÆ `int?`) also need `.Value` but existing code doesn't handle it. This is a pre-existing issue, not introduced by this task.

## 2026-02-28 ŌĆö Task 2.3.1: Create JsonDeserialize component (complete)

Created `src/components/serialization/JsonDeserialize.tsx` ŌĆö the core deserialization method skeleton for models implementing `IJsonModel<T>`.

**Changes:**
- New component `JsonDeserialize` generates `internal static {Model} Deserialize{Model}(JsonElement element, ModelReaderWriterOptions options)` method
- Method includes null check: `if (element.ValueKind == JsonValueKind.Null) { return null; }`
- Children slot for subsequent tasks to add variable declarations (2.3.3), property matching loop (2.3.4), and constructor return (2.3.13)
- Wired into emitter.tsx as a child of `ModelSerializationFile` alongside `JsonModelWriteCore` and `DeserializationConstructor`
- Exported from `src/components/serialization/index.ts`

**Pattern generated:**
```csharp
internal static Widget DeserializeWidget(JsonElement element, ModelReaderWriterOptions options)
{
    if (element.ValueKind == JsonValueKind.Null)
    {
        return null;
    }
}
```

**Design decisions:**
- Used raw strings + `code` template interpolation (same pattern as `JsonModelWriteCore`) for Allman-style brace formatting control
- `JsonValueKind.Null` is raw text ŌĆö the `using System.Text.Json;` directive is auto-generated by referencing `SystemTextJson.JsonElement` in the method signature via builtin refkey
- No `JsonValueKind` builtin declaration needed since the namespace is already imported

**Tests added:** 6 new tests in `JsonDeserialize` describe block covering method signature, null check, using directive, derived models, class placement, and indentation.

**Unblocks:** Tasks 2.3.2 (null check), 2.3.3 (variable declarations), 2.4.1 (discriminator peek), 2.5.2 (explicit ClientResult operator), 2.6.2 (JsonModelCreateCore).

- Null checks for reference type items (string, model, collections); no null check for value types (int, bool)
- Nested collections handled recursively with shadowed `item` loop variable
- Children type from @alloy-js/core used to break circular type inference between renderValueWrite and renderArraySerialization

2026-02-28 ŌĆö Task 2.3.4: Implement property matching loop (complete)

Created `src/components/serialization/PropertyMatchingLoop.tsx` with:
- `PropertyMatchingLoop` component ŌĆö generates `foreach (var prop in element.EnumerateObject())` loop
- `getReadExpression(type)` ŌĆö maps SDK types to `prop.Value.Get{Type}()` expressions
- `computeMatchableProperties(model)` ŌĆö gets flat property list (base + own for derived models)

Supported primitive types: string, boolean, int8-int64, uint8-uint64, float32, float64, decimal, decimal128, safeint, numeric, integer, url.
Unsupported types (return null, handled by 2.3.5-2.3.12): models, enums, collections, dicts, bytes, datetime, duration.

Pattern generated for each property:
```csharp
if (prop.NameEquals("serializedName"u8))
{
    varName = prop.Value.GetXxx();
    continue;
}
```

Design decision: Mirrors write-side pattern (PropertySerializer.tsx). Single component with helper function. Types not yet supported return null and are skipped, allowing incremental extension by subsequent tasks.

Integration: Added as child of `<JsonDeserialize>` after `<DeserializeVariableDeclarations>` in emitter.tsx.

15 new tests added to model-serialization.test.ts covering: foreach loop generation, primitive type getters (string/int/bool/float/url), multiple properties in order, serializedName usage, continue statements, derived model base property inclusion, indentation, placement after variable declarations.

## 2026-02-28 ŌĆö Task 2.3.6: Implement encoded type deserialization (complete)

Extended `getReadExpression()` in `PropertyMatchingLoop.tsx` with encoding-aware deserialization for:

**DateTime** (utcDateTime, offsetDateTime):
- rfc3339 (default) ŌåÆ `prop.Value.GetDateTimeOffset("O")`
- rfc7231 ŌåÆ `prop.Value.GetDateTimeOffset("R")`
- unixTimestamp ŌåÆ `DateTimeOffset.FromUnixTimeSeconds(prop.Value.GetInt64())`

**Duration**:
- ISO8601 (default) ŌåÆ `prop.Value.GetTimeSpan("P")`
- seconds + int32 wire ŌåÆ `TimeSpan.FromSeconds(prop.Value.GetInt32())`
- seconds + float wire ŌåÆ `TimeSpan.FromSeconds(prop.Value.GetDouble())`
- milliseconds + int32 wire ŌåÆ `TimeSpan.FromMilliseconds(prop.Value.GetInt32())`
- milliseconds + float wire ŌåÆ `TimeSpan.FromMilliseconds(prop.Value.GetDouble())`

**Bytes** (maps to BinaryData):
- base64 (default for bytes in TCGC) ŌåÆ `BinaryData.FromBytes(prop.Value.GetBytesFromBase64("D"))`
- base64url ŌåÆ `BinaryData.FromBytes(prop.Value.GetBytesFromBase64("U"))`
- raw fallback ŌåÆ `BinaryData.FromString(prop.Value.GetRawText())`

**plainDate** ŌåÆ `prop.Value.GetDateTimeOffset("D")`
**plainTime** ŌåÆ `prop.Value.GetTimeSpan("T")`

Key patterns:
- Helper functions (`getDateTimeReadExpression`, `getDurationReadExpression`, `getBytesReadExpression`)
  mirror the serialization side's `getDateTimeWriteInfo`, `getDurationWriteInfo` pattern
- Duration wire type check: only `int32` uses `GetInt32()`; all other wire types use `GetDouble()`
  (matches legacy emitter's Duration_Seconds vs Duration_Seconds_Float/Double format distinction)
- TCGC defaults bytes to encode="base64", so the raw text fallback is defensive

Files modified: src/components/serialization/PropertyMatchingLoop.tsx, test/model-serialization.test.ts
12 new tests added covering all encoded type variants.

## 2026-02-28 ŌĆö Task 2.3.7: Implement model deserialization (complete)

Extended `getReadExpression()` in `PropertyMatchingLoop.tsx` with nested model deserialization support.

**Pattern**: `ModelName.DeserializeModelName(prop.Value, options)` ŌĆö each model type has a static
`DeserializeXxx` method that reads its own properties from a `JsonElement`. Nested model properties
delegate to the nested model's own deserialization method.

**Implementation**: Added `namePolicy` optional parameter to `getReadExpression()` and a model type
check (`kind === "model"`) that uses the name policy to get the PascalCase class name. The name policy
is passed from the `PropertyMatchingLoop` component where `useCSharpNamePolicy()` is available.

**Design decision**: Extended `getReadExpression()` rather than handling models at the component level.
This keeps expression-to-type mapping centralized in one function, consistent with how all other types
are handled. The alternative (component-level handling like PropertySerializer.tsx) was rejected because
it would duplicate the rendering template.

**Type compatibility note**: The `namePolicy` parameter uses `NamePolicy<string>` from `@alloy-js/core`
to be compatible with `NamePolicy<CSharpElements>` returned by `useCSharpNamePolicy()`. Using an inline
type like `{ getName(name: string, element: string): string }` causes TS incompatibility because
`CSharpElements | undefined` is narrower than `string`.

Files modified: src/components/serialization/PropertyMatchingLoop.tsx
Tests added: 3 tests covering required nested model, multiple nested models, and derived discriminated model.

## 2026-02-28 ŌĆö Task 2.3.8: Implement enum deserialization (complete)

Added enum deserialization to the JSON read path in PropertyMatchingLoop.tsx.

**Changes:**
- `src/components/serialization/PropertyMatchingLoop.tsx`:
  - Added `SdkEnumType` import from TCGC
  - Created `getEnumReadExpression()` function that handles both fixed and extensible enums:
    - Fixed enums: `prop.Value.Get{Type}().To{EnumName}()` (extension method)
    - Extensible enums: `new {EnumName}(prop.Value.Get{Type}())` (constructor)
  - Added `kind === "enum"` case to `getReadExpression()` between primitive and model handlers
  - Updated JSDoc to include enums in supported types, removed enum from unsupported list

- `test/model-serialization.test.ts`:
  - Added 5 new tests in PropertyMatchingLoop describe block:
    - String-backed fixed enum ŌåÆ `prop.Value.GetString().ToStatus()`
    - Int-backed fixed enum ŌåÆ `prop.Value.GetInt32().ToPriority()`
    - Float-backed fixed enum ŌåÆ `prop.Value.GetSingle().ToRating()`
    - String-backed extensible enum ŌåÆ `new Color(prop.Value.GetString())`
    - Int-backed extensible enum ŌåÆ `new Level(prop.Value.GetInt32())`

**Design decision:** Added `getEnumReadExpression()` as a private helper in PropertyMatchingLoop.tsx (same file), mirroring how `getEnumWriteInfo()` lives in PropertySerializer.tsx. The read path reuses READ_METHOD_MAP for the getter method selection, keeping the approach DRY.

**Key insight:** Enum deserialization is the inverse of serialization but NOT symmetric:
- Write: Fixed int enums use direct cast `(int)value`, but Read: uses extension method `GetInt32().ToEnum()`
- Write: Extensible string enums use `.ToString()`, but Read: uses constructor `new Enum(GetString())`

Total tests: 413 (all passing). 5 new tests added.

  ```csharp
  List<T> array = new List<T>();

  ```

2026-03-01 ŌĆö Task 2.2.10: Implement dictionary serialization (complete)

- Added `renderDictionarySerialization` function to PropertySerializer.tsx
- Mirrors the existing `renderArraySerialization` pattern for the write path
- Generates `WriteStartObject ŌåÆ foreach (var item in Dict) ŌåÆ WritePropertyName(item.Key) ŌåÆ serialize value ŌåÆ WriteEndObject`
- Uses `var` for foreach type (unlike arrays which use explicit types)
- Null checks for reference type values: `if (item.Value == null) { WriteNullValue(); continue; }`
- Depth-based variable naming: `item` (depth 0), `item0` (depth 1), `item1` (depth 2)
- Unlike arrays which shadow `item`, dicts need distinct names because outer `.Key`/`.Value` access continues in inner `foreach` expressions
- Added `renderDictionaryProperty` function for Optional guard wrapping (mirrors `renderCollectionProperty`)
- Updated `renderValueWrite` to dispatch dict types to `renderDictionarySerialization`
- Updated `WritePropertySerialization` component to handle `dict` type properties
- Handles nested dicts recursively, arrays inside dicts via delegation to `renderArraySerialization`
- Added `getDictItemVarName(depth)` helper function

2026-03-01 ŌĆö Task 2.1.4: Generate PersistableModel write/create methods (complete)

Created two new serialization components:
- `src/components/serialization/PersistableModelWriteCore.tsx` ŌĆö generates `PersistableModelWriteCore` method that serializes model to `BinaryData` via format dispatch (JSON "J" ŌåÆ `ModelReaderWriter.Write`)
- `src/components/serialization/PersistableModelCreateCore.tsx` ŌĆö generates `PersistableModelCreateCore` method that deserializes model from `BinaryData` via format dispatch (JSON "J" ŌåÆ `JsonDocument.Parse` ŌåÆ `Deserialize{Model}`)

Key design decisions:
- Two separate component files (following existing JsonModelWriteCore.tsx pattern)
- `getRootModelType(model)` utility exported from PersistableModelCreateCore for finding the root ancestor in inheritance chains. Used for return type of CreateCore on derived models.
- Root models: `protected virtual`, derived models: `protected override`
- Return type: WriteCore always returns `BinaryData`. CreateCore returns root base type for polymorphic compatibility.
- Deferred: `SampleTypeSpecContext.Default` parameter (task 5.3.1) and `ModelSerializationExtensions.JsonDocumentOptions` parameter (task 5.1.5) ŌĆö both are optional C# parameters

Wired into emitter.tsx between JsonModelWriteCore and DeserializationConstructor.

## 2026-03-01 ŌĆö Task 2.1.5: Generate explicit interface implementations (complete)

### What was done
- Created `src/components/serialization/PersistableModelInterfaceMethods.tsx` component
- Generates three explicit `IPersistableModel<T>` interface implementations:
  1. `BinaryData IPersistableModel<T>.Write(ModelReaderWriterOptions options) => PersistableModelWriteCore(options);`
  2. `T IPersistableModel<T>.Create(BinaryData data, ModelReaderWriterOptions options) => PersistableModelCreateCore(data, options);`
  3. `string IPersistableModel<T>.GetFormatFromOptions(ModelReaderWriterOptions options) => "J";`
- For derived models, Create method includes a cast: `(T)PersistableModelCreateCore(data, options)` because the virtual method returns the root base type
- Wired into emitter.tsx between PersistableModelCreateCore and DeserializationConstructor
- 6 tests added in test/persistable-model-interface.test.ts

### Design decision
- Used `code` templates with builtin refkeys (not Alloy Method component) because Alloy's Method component doesn't support explicit interface implementations (no `explicitInterface` prop)
- Follows the same pattern as PersistableModelWriteCore and PersistableModelCreateCore

### Notes for next iteration
- IJsonModel<T> explicit interface implementations are separate tasks (2.6.1 Write, 2.6.2 Create/JsonModelCreateCore)
- The IJsonModel<T>.Write method has a multi-line body (WriteStartObject ŌåÆ JsonModelWriteCore ŌåÆ WriteEndObject), not expression-bodied

- Smoke tests remain failing due to pre-existing issues (dotnet build and Union type)

2026-03-01 ŌĆö Task 11.1.5: Handle inline string literal union types in TypeExpression (complete)

Problem: The emitter crashed with "Unsupported type for TypeExpression: Union ("red" | "blue")" when a model property used an inline string literal union type. The upstream TypeExpression only handles named unions and nullable unions, but inline literal unions are unnamed.

Root cause: TCGC converts inline string literal unions to SdkEnumType, and the emitter generates enum files for them. But when ModelProperty passes type.__raw! to TypeExpression, the raw type is an unnamed TypeSpec Union, which TypeExpression doesn't know how to handle.

Fix: Added a `forTypeKind("Union", ...)` override in CSharpTypeExpression.tsx using the existing Experimental_ComponentOverridesConfig pattern. The override:
- Delegates named unions and nullable unions to the default TypeExpression
- For unnamed non-nullable unions (inline literal unions), emits a <Reference refkey={efCsharpRefkey(union)} /> that resolves to the generated enum declaration

Key design decision: Used the override mechanism rather than fixing individual callsites (ModelProperty, serialization, etc.) because:
1. Centralizes the fix for ALL TypeExpression usages
2. Follows the existing pattern (scalar and intrinsic overrides are already there)
3. The enum file declarations already register efCsharpRefkey(rawType) as their refkey

Files changed:
- src/components/CSharpTypeExpression.tsx ŌĆö Added Union override and hasNullVariant helper
- test/model.test.ts ŌĆö Added test for inline string literal union type resolution

Pattern: The override mechanism in CSharpTypeExpression.tsx now handles three type kinds: Union, Scalar, and Intrinsic. Future type expression overrides should follow the same pattern.

2026-03-01 ŌĆö Task 11.1.6: Fix array deserialization to call .ToArray() (complete)

Problem: Generated deserialization code assigns a List<T> directly to a T[]-typed variable without calling .ToArray(), causing CS0029 type mismatch errors.

Root cause: PropertyMatchingLoop.tsx builds a List<T> during array deserialization but DeserializeVariableDeclarations.tsx declares variables with TypeExpression which renders arrays as T[].

Fix: Added .ToArray() in three locations in PropertyMatchingLoop.tsx:
1. Top-level array property assignment: `varName = array.ToArray();`
2. Nested array added to outer list: `arrayVar.Add(innerArrayVar.ToArray());`
3. Array inside dictionary: `dictVar.Add(propVar.Name, array.ToArray());`

Updated 6 test expectations in model-serialization.test.ts to match the corrected output.

Result: 5 additional tests now pass (484 vs 479 before). All 6 remaining failures are pre-existing and unrelated.

Pattern: When List<T> is used as an intermediate collection during deserialization, always call .ToArray() before assigning to a T[]-typed variable or adding to a collection that expects T[].

2026-03-01 ŌĆö Task 1.1.3: Create collection type utilities (complete)

Created `src/utils/collections.ts` with pure utility functions for C# collection type determination:
- `getCollectionPropertyVariant(type, isReadOnly)` ŌĆö determines IList/IReadOnlyList/IDictionary/IReadOnlyDictionary based on read-only status
- `getCollectionParameterVariant(type)` ŌĆö determines IEnumerable (arrays) or IDictionary (dicts) for constructor params
- `getCollectionValueType(type)` ŌĆö extracts element/value type from collections
- `isArrayCollection(type)` / `isDictCollection(type)` ŌĆö type guards

Matches legacy emitter's 3-layer system:
1. TypeFactory.CreateCSharpType ŌåÆ IList<T>, IDictionary<string,T>
2. CSharpType.GetOutputType ŌåÆ IReadOnlyList<T>, IReadOnlyDictionary<string,T>
3. CSharpType.GetInputType ŌåÆ IEnumerable<T> for array parameters

Key design decision: Pure utility functions (no JSX, no Alloy deps) returning string identifiers. Components use these with `code` template tags and Alloy Generic.* library references for rendering. Follows the same pattern as property.ts and nullable.ts.

Test: 32 tests in test/collections.test.ts covering all variants, nullable unwrapping, error cases, and cross-function consistency.

Next: Task 1.1.5 (type mapping tests) is now unblocked by this work.

## 2026-03-01 ŌĆö Tasks 2.4.1/2.4.2/2.4.3: Implement discriminator deserialization dispatch (complete)

Created `src/components/serialization/DiscriminatorDeserialization.tsx` ŌĆö a new component that generates
the discriminator dispatch block for models with discriminated subtypes:
- Peeks at discriminator property via `element.TryGetProperty("{name}"u8, out JsonElement discriminator)`
- Switches on `discriminator.GetString()` to dispatch to derived type deserializers
- Falls back to `Unknown{Base}.Deserialize{Unknown}(element, options)` for unrecognized values

Modified `JsonDeserialize.tsx` to conditionally render the discriminator dispatch for models with
`hasDiscriminatedSubtypes()` instead of the standard body (variable declarations + property matching + return).

Tasks 2.4.1/2.4.2/2.4.3 implemented together as one atomic change since peek, switch, and fallback are
inseparable ŌĆö an empty switch doesn't compile, and without the fallback there's no return path.

Updated 3 existing tests that verified the OLD incorrect behavior (standard body for discriminated base models)
and added 3 new tests for the correct discriminator dispatch behavior.

Key patterns:
- `model.discriminatorProperty.serializedName` gives the JSON property name for TryGetProperty
- `model.discriminatedSubtypes` is a flat Record<string, SdkModelType> of all descendant subtypes
- Unknown variant name follows pattern `Unknown{BaseName}`

## 2026-03-01 ŌĆö Task 2.3.11: Implement null value handling (complete)

Modified `src/components/serialization/PropertyMatchingLoop.tsx` to handle `JsonValueKind.Null` during JSON deserialization.

**Changes:**
- Added `NullCheckBehavior` type and `getNullCheckBehavior(property)` function that determines the null-handling strategy for each property variant
- Added `renderPropertyNullCheck(behavior, varName, property)` function that generates the C# null-check block
- Added `itemNeedsNullCheck(rawItemType)` helper for collection element null checks
- Modified `PropertyMatchingLoop` component to insert property-level null checks before value extraction
- Modified `renderArrayDeserialization` to add if/else null checks for nullable array items
- Modified `renderDictionaryDeserialization` to add if/else null checks for nullable dict values
- Imported `isCollectionType` and `isPropertyNullable` from nullable utils
- Created `test/null-value-handling.test.ts` with 15 tests: 11 unit tests for `getNullCheckBehavior` and 4 integration tests

**Three property-level null check behaviors:**
1. `assign-null` ŌĆö nullable non-collection: `propVar = null; continue;`
2. `skip` ŌĆö optional collection: `continue;` (leave ChangeTracking default)
3. `empty-collection` ŌĆö required nullable collection: `propVar = new ChangeTrackingList<T>(); continue;`

**Item-level null checks:**
- Only generated when `valueType.kind === "nullable"` (TCGC marks items explicitly nullable)
- Arrays: `if (item.ValueKind == JsonValueKind.Null) { array.Add(null); } else { array.Add(value); }`
- Dicts: `if (prop0.Value.ValueKind == JsonValueKind.Null) { dictionary.Add(prop0.Name, null); } else { ... }`

**Patterns used:** Inline rendering in PropertyMatchingLoop (no separate component), raw string templates for JsonValueKind.Null (already has `using System.Text.Json` from other serialization code), TypeExpression for ChangeTracking generic parameters.

**Tests:** 549 passing (15 new), 6 pre-existing failures (model-serialization XML, nested dict depth, 4 smoke tests).

## 2026-03-01 ŌĆö Task 3.2.1: Create ClientFile component

### What was done
- Created `src/components/clients/ClientFile.tsx` ŌĆö generates C# partial class files for both root and sub-clients
- Created `src/utils/clients.ts` ŌĆö `getAllClients()` utility that flattens the TCGC client tree (BFS traversal)
- Added `Uri` to `src/builtins/system.ts` for endpoint field type references
- Updated `src/emitter.tsx` to render ClientFile for all clients (root + sub-clients)
- Created `test/client-file.test.ts` with 6 tests covering root clients, sub-clients, doc comments, and edge cases

### Generated output structure
For sub-clients:
```csharp
public partial class SubClient {
    private readonly Uri _endpoint;
    protected SubClient() { }
    internal SubClient(ClientPipeline pipeline, Uri endpoint) { _endpoint = endpoint; Pipeline = pipeline; }
    public ClientPipeline Pipeline { get; }
}
```
Root clients get: endpoint field, mocking constructor, Pipeline property. Primary constructors (with auth) deferred to task 3.2.3.

### Patterns used
- `OverloadConstructor` from ModelConstructors.tsx for multiple constructors in same class (avoids Alloy name conflicts)
- `getAllClients()` BFS traversal because `sdkPackage.clients` only contains root-level clients; sub-clients are in `.children`
- `System.Uri` builtin for auto-generating `using System;` directives
- Root vs sub-client detection: `client.parent !== undefined`
- Doc comment: root uses `client.doc ?? client.summary`, sub-client uses "The {Name} sub-client."

### What the next person should know
- TCGC does NOT produce clients for `@service namespace X;` without operations ŌĆö no client file is generated for empty services
- Tasks 3.2.2/3.2.3/3.2.4 will modify ClientFile to add auth fields, primary constructors, and sub-client factory methods
- The `{props.children}` slot in ClientFile goes after the Pipeline property ŌĆö good for injecting operation methods
- Pre-existing failures: smoke tests (4) and model-serialization (2) are unrelated

## 2026-03-01 ŌĆö Task 3.2.2: Implement client fields

### What was done
- Added `AuthenticationTokenProvider` builtin to `src/builtins/system-client-model.ts`
- Created `src/utils/client-params.ts` with utility functions for extracting client parameter info from TCGC:
  - `getAuthInfo(client)` ŌĆö extracts API key and OAuth2 auth scheme details
  - `getClientMethodParameters(client)` ŌĆö returns non-endpoint, non-credential method params
  - `getEndpointParameter(client)` ŌĆö extracts the endpoint parameter
  - `getFieldTypeForParam(param)` ŌĆö maps TCGC SDK types to C# type names
- Modified `src/components/clients/ClientFile.tsx` to generate all client fields:
  - API key auth fields: `_keyCredential` (ApiKeyCredential), `AuthorizationHeader` (const string)
  - OAuth2 auth fields: `_tokenProvider` (AuthenticationTokenProvider), `AuthorizationScopes` (static readonly string[])
  - Method parameter fields (e.g., `_apiVersion`) as private readonly
  - Sub-client caching fields (e.g., `_cachedPetOperations`) ŌĆö NOT readonly, for lazy init
- Added `refkey(client)` to ClassDeclaration for cross-file type references (sub-client cache fields)
- Added 6 new tests covering all field types, ordering, and sub-client auth exclusion

### Key patterns
- Auth fields are ONLY on root clients (no parent). Sub-clients inherit auth through the pipeline.
- Const fields (AuthorizationHeader) use raw strings since Alloy's Field component doesn't support `const`.
- Sub-client cache fields reference child client types via `refkey(child)` for cross-file resolution.
- API version field type is always `string` regardless of TCGC's underlying type (matches legacy behavior).
- Field order matches legacy: endpoint ŌåÆ auth ŌåÆ method params ŌåÆ cache fields.

### TCGC notes
- `client.clientInitialization.parameters` includes endpoint, credential, and method params
- API version shows up as a method param with `isApiVersionParam: true` when the TypeSpec has `@query apiVersion: string`
- For versioned services without explicit apiVersion param, TCGC may not include it in init params
- `Oauth2Auth` in @typespec/http uses lowercase 'a' (not `OAuth2Auth`)
- `Oauth2Auth` takes 1 type argument (not 2)
- SdkBuiltInKinds does NOT include uuid, password, eTag, ipV4Address, etc. ŌĆö only TypeSpec intrinsic scalar names

### Pre-existing failures (not related to this task)
- model-serialization.test.ts: 2 failures
- smoke.test.ts: 4 failures

2026-03-02 ŌĆö Task 1.8.4: Handle discriminator exclusion in factory (complete)

Added discriminator exclusion logic to `ModelFactoryMethod.tsx`:
- New `getDiscriminatorLiteral()` helper walks the model hierarchy to find the correct discriminator value for each discriminator property. Handles both string discriminators (`"cat"`) and enum discriminators (`PetKind.Cat`).
- Multi-level hierarchies (Pet ŌåÆ Fish ŌåÆ Shark) correctly map each discriminator property to the value from the appropriate level.
- Changed `ctorArgs` from `string[]` to `Children[]` to support enum discriminator refkeys (which need Alloy to auto-generate `using` directives).
- Constructor args now joined with flatMap instead of `.join()` to handle mixed Children types.

Key pattern: The discriminator detection check is `p.discriminator === true` followed by `getDiscriminatorLiteral()` returning non-undefined. This correctly handles:
- Derived models (Cat with discriminatorValue="cat"): discriminator excluded, literal injected
- Abstract base models (Pet with no discriminatorValue): discriminator kept as parameter
- Intermediate hierarchy models: each discriminator maps to correct level's value

Test added: `excludes discriminator from factory params for derived models` ŌĆö verifies Cat's factory method signature excludes `kind`, injects `"cat"` literal, while Pet's method correctly keeps `kind`.

Pre-existing failures: 4 smoke tests (dotnet build config), 2 model-serialization tests (unrelated).

## 2026-03-02 ŌĆö Task 3.3.1: Create RestClientFile component (complete)

### What was done
Created `src/components/clients/RestClientFile.tsx` ŌĆö generates `{ClassName}.RestClient.cs` partial class files with:
- Static `PipelineMessageClassifier` fields with lazy `??=` initialization per unique set of success status codes
- `Create{Op}Request` methods for each HTTP operation on the client

### Method body pattern
Each CreateRequest method follows the System.ClientModel pattern:
1. `ClientUriBuilder uri = new ClientUriBuilder();` + `uri.Reset(_endpoint);`
2. Path segments via `uri.AppendPath(literal, false)` and `uri.AppendPath(param, true)`
3. Query params via `uri.AppendQuery(serializedName, value, true)` with null checks for optional
4. `PipelineMessage message = Pipeline.CreateMessage(uri.ToUri(), "VERB", classifier);`
5. `PipelineRequest request = message.Request;`
6. Custom headers ŌåÆ Content-Type (from body) ŌåÆ Accept (from responses)
7. `request.Content = content;` (if body)
8. `message.Apply(options);` + `return message;`

### Key patterns and decisions
- **Partial class**: Uses `namekey(className, { ignoreNameConflict: true })` ŌĆö same pattern as ModelSerializationFile ŌĆö to avoid Alloy's symbol deduplication renaming
- **Type mapping**: Direct switch-based mapping from SdkType.kind to C# types (not TypeExpression, which expects TypeSpec `Type` not SdkType). Returns strings for keywords (string, int), refkeys for types needing `using` (DateTimeOffset, Uri, BinaryData)
- **Parameter ordering**: path (0) ŌåÆ required header/query (100) ŌåÆ body (200/300) ŌåÆ optional header/query (400) ŌåÆ RequestOptions (always last)
- **ClientUriBuilder/TypeFormatters**: Raw strings, not builtins ŌĆö they're internal types in the same namespace
- **Constants**: Params with `type.kind === "constant"` are hardcoded in method body, not method params
- **Client fields**: Params with `onClient: true` (apiVersion, etc.) use class field references like `_apiVersion`
- **Content-Type**: Derived from `bodyParam.defaultContentType`, not a method parameter
- **Accept**: Derived from response `defaultContentType`/`contentTypes`

### Files created/modified
- CREATE: `src/components/clients/RestClientFile.tsx`
- CREATE: `test/rest-client.test.ts` (11 tests)
- MODIFY: `src/emitter.tsx` (add RestClientFile to component tree)
- MODIFY: `src/builtins/system.ts` (add DateTimeOffset and TimeSpan to System builtin)

### Builtins added
- `System.DateTimeOffset` (struct) ŌĆö for utcDateTime/offsetDateTime parameter types
- `System.TimeSpan` (struct) ŌĆö for duration parameter types

### What's next
- Task 3.3.2: Implement request building (next-link pagination methods, complex path expressions)
- Task 3.3.3: Implement parameter serialization variants (collection formats, encoding-specific formatting)

## 2026-03-02 ŌĆö Task 3.4.1: Create ProtocolMethod component (complete)

### What was done
Created `src/components/clients/ProtocolMethod.tsx` ŌĆö generates sync/async protocol method pairs in the ClientFile class for each HTTP operation.

### Generated pattern
Each HTTP operation produces two methods:
1. **Sync**: `public virtual ClientResult {Name}(...params, RequestOptions options)`
2. **Async**: `public virtual async Task<ClientResult> {Name}Async(...params, RequestOptions options)`

Method body follows the `using PipelineMessage` pattern:
```csharp
Argument.AssertNotNullOrEmpty(id, nameof(id));  // string params
Argument.AssertNotNull(content, nameof(content)); // reference type params

using PipelineMessage message = Create{Name}Request(params, options);
return ClientResult.FromResponse(Pipeline.ProcessMessage(message, options));
// async: await Pipeline.ProcessMessageAsync(message, options).ConfigureAwait(false)
```

### Key patterns and decisions
- **XML docs**: `[Protocol Method]` prefix + `<see href="https://aka.ms/azsdk/net/protocol-methods">` link + exception docs for ArgumentNullException, ArgumentException, ClientResultException
- **Parameter ordering**: Same as CreateRequest (path ŌåÆ required ŌåÆ body ŌåÆ optional ŌåÆ options). Reuses same priority-based sorting logic from RestClientFile.
- **Parameter defaults**: Optional params get `= default`, RequestOptions gets `= null` when optional params exist
- **Validation**: String params ŌåÆ `Argument.AssertNotNullOrEmpty`, BinaryContent/other ŌåÆ `Argument.AssertNotNull`. Only required params validated.
- **Task<> return type**: Added `SystemThreadingTasks` library to builtins for auto-generating `using System.Threading.Tasks;`
- **Access modifier**: Supports `public` (default) and `internal` from `SdkServiceMethod.access`
- **Integration**: ProtocolMethods rendered inside ClientFile's ClassDeclaration, before SubClientFactoryMethods

### Files changed
- **Created**: `src/components/clients/ProtocolMethod.tsx` (main component)
- **Created**: `test/protocol-method.test.ts` (9 tests)
- **Modified**: `src/builtins/system-threading.ts` (added SystemThreadingTasks for Task<>)
- **Modified**: `src/builtins/index.ts` (exported SystemThreadingTasks)
- **Modified**: `src/components/clients/ClientFile.tsx` (render ProtocolMethods)

### What's next
- Task 3.4.2: Write protocol method tests (already done as part of this task)
- Task 3.5.1: Create ConvenienceMethod component (depends on 3.4.1)
- Task 3.3.2: Implement request building enhancements (next-link pagination, complex paths)

## 2026-03-02 ŌĆö Task 3.5.1: Create ConvenienceMethod component (complete)

**What was done:**
Created `src/components/clients/ConvenienceMethod.tsx` ŌĆö generates sync/async convenience method pairs that delegate to protocol methods with typed parameters and return types.

**Generated pattern:**
Each HTTP operation where `generateConvenient === true` produces two methods:
1. **Sync**: `public virtual ClientResult<T> {Name}(...params, CancellationToken cancellationToken = default)`
2. **Async**: `public virtual async Task<ClientResult<T>> {Name}Async(...params, CancellationToken cancellationToken = default)`

For void return operations, returns `ClientResult` (no generic type parameter).

**Key patterns and decisions:**
- **Typed parameters**: Uses `TypeExpression` for model/enum types, keyword mapping for primitives (same as protocol but without enum unwrapping)
- **Body params**: Passed directly to protocol method ŌĆö C# implicit operator converts model ŌåÆ BinaryContent
- **Enum params**: Converted via `.ToString()` for string-backed enums, cast for int-backed
- **Response wrapping**: `ClientResult.FromValue((T)result, result.GetRawResponse())` ŌĆö uses explicit cast operator on model
- **CancellationToken**: Converted to `RequestOptions` via `.ToRequestOptions()` extension method
- **Validation**: Only reference types get `Argument.Assert*` ŌĆö value types (int, enum, DateTime, etc.) skip validation
- **Name conflict fix**: Used `namekey(name, { ignoreNameConflict: true })` on both convenience AND protocol Method components to allow C# method overloading without Alloy's `_2` suffix
- **XML docs**: Simple summary (no [Protocol Method] prefix), CancellationToken docs, exception docs

**Files changed:**
- Created: `src/components/clients/ConvenienceMethod.tsx` (main component, 9 tests)
- Created: `test/convenience-method.test.ts` (9 tests)
- Modified: `src/builtins/system-threading.ts` (added CancellationToken builtin)
- Modified: `src/components/clients/ClientFile.tsx` (integrated ConvenienceMethods before ProtocolMethods)
- Modified: `src/components/clients/ProtocolMethod.tsx` (added namekey with ignoreNameConflict)

**What's next:** Task 3.5.2 (spread parameter handling), Task 3.6.1 (operation name conventions)

## 2026-03-02 ŌĆö Task 2.4.5: Write discriminated deserialization tests

Created `test/discriminator-deserialization.test.ts` with 5 test cases covering:

1. **Enum discriminator dispatch on base model** ŌĆö verifies TryGetProperty + switch + Unknown fallback pattern works identically for enum discriminators as for string discriminators. Case values are strings (JSON serialized form).

2. **Enum discriminator variable initialization in derived model** ŌĆö verifies enum discriminator variables use `default` (not enum literal), matching legacy emitter behavior where only string-typed discriminators get literal init.

3. **Multi-level hierarchy root dispatch** ŌĆö verifies Fish (root base) dispatches to Shark (kind="shark") and Salmon (kind="salmon") but NOT to SawShark (which uses a different discriminator property "sharktype").

4. **Intermediate model dispatch** ŌĆö verifies Shark (intermediate: has both discriminatorValue AND own subtypes) uses discriminator dispatch on its own "sharktype" property, with UnknownShark fallback.

5. **Leaf model standard deserialization** ŌĆö verifies SawShark (leaf) uses standard property matching loop. Documents known behavior where nested discriminator variables all get initialized to model.discriminatorValue.

Key findings:
- discriminatedSubtypes map is NOT flat across different discriminator properties ŌĆö each level only contains entries for its own discriminator.
- Nested discriminators: all string discriminator variables get initialized to model.discriminatorValue regardless of which discriminator property they belong to (bug-compatible with legacy emitter).
- TypeSpec requires different discriminator property names at each level (reusing same @discriminator on child causes diagnostics).

## 2026-03-02 ŌĆö Task 11.1.1: Add missing using directives in generated model files (complete)

### What was done
- Created `src/builtins/system-collections-generic.ts` with `IDictionary` library declaration using `createLibrary("System.Collections.Generic", {...})`
- Updated `src/components/models/ModelFile.tsx` to use `code` template with `SystemCollectionsGeneric.IDictionary` and `System.BinaryData` refkeys instead of raw string for the `_additionalBinaryDataProperties` field declaration
- Updated `src/components/models/ModelConstructors.tsx` to use refkey-based JSX expression instead of raw string `"IDictionary<string, BinaryData>"` for the serialization constructor parameter type
- Updated `src/components/serialization/DeserializeVariableDeclarations.tsx` to use `SystemCollectionsGeneric.IDictionary` refkey instead of raw string in the deserialization variable declaration
- Added test assertions in `test/model.test.ts` for `using System;` and `using System.Collections.Generic;` in model files

### Key design decision
Used refkeys in `code` templates (Option A) rather than explicit `using` prop on `SourceFile` (Option B). This follows the existing pattern (e.g., `System.BinaryData` refkey) and lets Alloy auto-manage using directives. New builtins follow the project convention: one `createLibrary()` call per namespace in a dedicated file under `src/builtins/`.

### Pattern established
When types like `IDictionary`, `BinaryData`, etc. appear in raw string literals or `code` templates, always use refkeys from the builtin libraries instead. This triggers Alloy's automatic `using` directive generation. The builtin file naming convention is `system-{namespace-suffix}.ts` (e.g., `system-collections-generic.ts`).

### Notes for next iteration
- 6 pre-existing test failures remain (4 smoke tests with preprocessor directive issue in AdditionalBinaryDataWrite output, 2 model serialization tests)
- The smoke test build errors are caused by `#else` preprocessor directive being on the same line as `using` statement in generated serialization code ŌĆö this is a separate formatting bug

## 2026-03-02 ŌĆö Task 3.6.1: Implement operation name conventions (complete)

**What was done:**
- Created `src/utils/operation-naming.ts` with `cleanOperationName()` utility function
- Implements .NET convention: "List" ŌåÆ "GetAll", "ListXxx" ŌåÆ "GetXxx" (matching legacy `GetCleanOperationName` in `ClientProvider.cs`)
- Applied the transformation in all three files that resolve operation names:
  - `ProtocolMethod.tsx` ŌĆö sync/async protocol method names
  - `ConvenienceMethod.tsx` ŌĆö sync/async convenience method names  
  - `RestClientFile.tsx` ŌĆö `Create{Name}Request` method names
- Created comprehensive test suite in `test/operation-naming.test.ts` (11 tests):
  - Unit tests for the `cleanOperationName` function (edge cases: Listen, Listed, exact "List")
  - Integration tests verifying the full emitter pipeline produces correct renamed output
  - Tests for protocol methods, convenience methods, and REST client CreateRequest methods
  - Negative tests ensuring non-List operations are not renamed

**Design decision:**
- Chose to create a standalone utility function rather than modifying the naming policy, because:
  1. The naming policy is from `@alloy-js/csharp` (generic) ŌĆö this is domain-specific logic
  2. Matches the legacy emitter's architecture (standalone `GetCleanOperationName` function)
  3. Explicitly visible where it's used, easy to grep/test
- The function takes PascalCase input (after namePolicy.getName) and applies ListŌåÆGet transformation
- All three consumer files import and apply it at the same point in the pipeline

**Pattern:** `cleanOperationName(namePolicy.getName(method.name, "class"))` ŌĆö always apply cleanOperationName AFTER the naming policy.

## 2026-03-02 ŌĆö Task 3.3.3: Implement parameter serialization variants (complete)

### What was done
Implemented collection parameter serialization in RestClientFile.tsx for all parameter placement variants:

1. **Collection query parameters**: CSV (AppendQueryDelimited with ","), SSV (" "), Pipes ("|"), Multi/explode (foreach loop with AppendQuery per element)
2. **Collection path parameters**: AppendPathDelimited with comma delimiter for array path params
3. **Collection header parameters**: string.Join for combining collection values into single header
4. **Path URL encoding control**: allowReserved flag (from RFC 6570 `+` operator) controls the `escape` parameter (false when allowReserved=true)

### Files changed
- `src/builtins/system-collections-generic.ts` ŌĆö Added IEnumerable interface for collection parameter types
- `src/components/clients/RestClientFile.tsx` ŌĆö Added helpers: isCollectionType, getCollectionDelimiter, isExplodedQueryParam, buildQueryParamStatement, buildPathParamStatement, buildHeaderParamStatement. Updated getProtocolTypeExpression for array types (ŌåÆ IEnumerable<T>). Refactored buildRequestBody to use new helpers.
- `test/rest-client.test.ts` ŌĆö Added 6 new tests covering: CSV delimited query, exploded query, optional collection query, optional exploded query, path allowReserved, collection header

### Patterns used
- `IEnumerable<T>` for collection parameter types in method signatures (via SystemCollectionsGeneric.IEnumerable refkey for auto-using)
- `code` template with refkeys for generating C# type expressions with automatic using directives
- `@query(#{explode: true})` for multi format in TypeSpec
- `@route("/files/{+path}")` for allowReserved via RFC 6570 + operator

### Key learnings
- TypeSpec HTTP decorators only support `explode: boolean` ŌĆö pipes/SSV/TSV formats come from OpenAPI3 import scenarios, not native TypeSpec
- Path allowReserved must be expressed via URI template syntax ({+var}), not @path decorator options
- The `code` tag with `\n` separators in Children arrays produces correct semantic output (Alloy handles indentation) even though raw output may look compressed
- TCGC sets collectionFormat based on TypeSpec's explode flag: explode=false ŌåÆ "csv", explode=true ŌåÆ "multi"

### Next person should know
- Pipes/SSV/TSV collection formats are implemented but can't be tested directly with TypeSpec syntax (only via OpenAPI3 imports)
- The formatting of multi-line statements (foreach, if blocks) in the generated code has some compression issues (closing brace on same line as next statement) ŌĆö this is a pre-existing Alloy rendering behavior, not introduced by this change

### Patterns used
- `<SourceFile>` from `@alloy-js/csharp` with `using` prop for explicit using directives
- `<Namespace>` for dynamic namespace from packageName
- `<ClassDeclaration>` for simple classes (Argument, Optional, ChangeTrackingList)
- Raw `code` template for ChangeTrackingDictionary's full class body (workaround for Alloy TypeParameterConstraints bug that generates empty `where TValue :` constraint when only TKey has constraints)
- `code` template tag from `@alloy-js/core` for method bodies within ClassDeclaration ŌĆö handles indentation automatically

### Key learnings
- Alloy's `code` template tag handles multi-line C# code with proper indentation ŌĆö it detects relative indentation from leading whitespace and creates `<indent>` nodes
- `<ClassDeclaration>` `typeParameters` with constraints triggers rendering for ALL type params, even those without constraints ŌĆö causes invalid `where TValue :` output when mixing constrained/unconstrained params. Workaround: use raw `code` template for the full class declaration
- Infrastructure files are always generated (not conditional on models/clients) matching legacy emitter behavior
- `<SourceFile>` `using` prop accepts array of namespace strings for explicit using directives

### Next person should know
- The infrastructure files are rendered OUTSIDE of `<CSharpScalarOverrides>` in the emitter tree since they don't reference TypeSpec types
- The ChangeTrackingDictionary uses a different rendering approach (raw code template) than the other three (ClassDeclaration) ŌĆö this is intentional due to the Alloy TypeParameterConstraints limitation
- Tasks 5.1.1-5.1.4 in the PRD overlap with parts of this task ŌĆö they may need to be marked as done or their scope reviewed

## 2026-03-02 ŌĆö Task 5.2.1: Generate CodeGen attribute files

### What was done
- Created `src/components/infrastructure/CodeGenAttributeFiles.tsx` with 4 internal file components:
  - `CodeGenTypeAttribute.cs` ŌĆö Base attribute marking types with original names (targets Class/Enum/Struct)
  - `CodeGenMemberAttribute.cs` ŌĆö Marks property/field members with original names (extends CodeGenTypeAttribute)
  - `CodeGenSuppressAttribute.cs` ŌĆö Suppresses specific generated members (AllowMultiple = true)
  - `CodeGenSerializationAttribute.cs` ŌĆö Configures custom serialization hooks (AllowMultiple + Inherited)
- Updated `src/emitter.tsx` to render CodeGenAttributeFiles in every generated project
