- Created `test/codegen-attributes.test.ts` with 18 comprehensive tests
- Also marked tasks 5.1.1-5.1.4 as done (already implemented in prior loop 11.1.3)

### Patterns used
- Single parent component (`CodeGenAttributeFiles`) rendering 4 child file components
- `ClassDeclaration` with `baseType` prop for inheritance (not `extends`)
- `attributes` prop for `[AttributeUsage(...)]` decorators (not `decorators`)
- `code` template tag for static method bodies
- Fixed namespace: `Microsoft.TypeSpec.Generator.Customizations` (NOT derived from packageName)

### Key learnings & Next person should know
- CodeGen attribute files use a HARDCODED namespace `Microsoft.TypeSpec.Generator.Customizations`, not the package namespace. This matches `CodeModelGenerator.CustomizationAttributeNamespace` in the legacy emitter.
- ClassDeclaration prop for base class is `baseType` (not `extends`)
- ClassDeclaration prop for attribute annotations is `attributes` (not `decorators`)
- When adding new Internal/ files, check existing tests that filter by partial path/name ŌĆö e.g., `k.includes("Serialization")` will match infrastructure files. Add `!k.includes("Internal/")` to exclude them.

2026-03-02 ŌĆö Task 0.2.3: Add SCM paging builtins (complete)

Added paging-related types to the System.ClientModel builtins in `src/builtins/system-client-model.ts`:
- `CollectionResult` (class) ŌĆö abstract base for sync pagination, with `GetContinuationToken` method
- `AsyncCollectionResult` (class) ŌĆö abstract base for async pagination, with `GetContinuationToken` method
- `ContinuationToken` (class) ŌĆö opaque pagination token, with `FromBytes` static factory method

All three types are in the `System.ClientModel` namespace (not Primitives). They're declared as classes
following the same pattern as existing SCM builtins (ClientResult, BinaryContent, etc.).

Generic variants (CollectionResult<T>, AsyncCollectionResult<T>) don't need separate declarations ŌĆö
Alloy handles generics syntactically via code templates: `code\`${SystemClientModel.CollectionResult}<${T}>\``.
This matches how IJsonModel and IPersistableModel handle their generic parameter.

Added tests in `test/builtins.test.tsx`:
- Type declaration tests: verify all three types and their members are defined
- Using statement test: verify referencing paging types produces `using System.ClientModel;`

This task unblocks 4.1.1 (CollectionResultFile component) and the full paging chain (4.2.1, 4.3.1, 4.4.1, 4.4.2).

## 2026-03-02 ŌĆö Task 4.1.1: Create CollectionResultFile component (complete)

Created `src/components/collection-results/CollectionResultFile.tsx` ŌĆö the core paging collection result component.

**What it does:**
- `CollectionResultFiles` component iterates over paging methods (kind === "paging") on a client
- For each paging operation, generates 4 source files (sync/async ├Ś protocol/convenience):
  - `{Client}{Op}CollectionResult` ŌĆö extends `CollectionResult`, sync protocol
  - `{Client}{Op}CollectionResultOfT` ŌĆö extends `CollectionResult<T>`, sync convenience with `GetValuesFromPage`
  - `{Client}{Op}AsyncCollectionResult` ŌĆö extends `AsyncCollectionResult`, async protocol
  - `{Client}{Op}AsyncCollectionResultOfT` ŌĆö extends `AsyncCollectionResult<T>`, async convenience with `GetValuesFromPageAsync`

**Implementation details:**
- Uses `useCSharpNamePolicy()` and `cleanOperationName()` for consistent naming
- Base type is `SystemClientModel.CollectionResult` / `SystemClientModel.AsyncCollectionResult`
- Convenience variants use `<TypeExpression type={sdkType.__raw!} />` for item type and response model type references
- Item type and property path extracted from `method.pagingMetadata.pageItemsSegments`
- Response model type from `method.operation.responses`
- Async convenience uses foreach/yield return/await Task.Yield() pattern
- XML doc comments on all members

**Paging strategy:**
- Currently implements single-page strategy (simple yield return, GetContinuationToken returns null)
- Tasks 4.2.1 and 4.3.1 will extend GetRawPages with while loops for next-link and continuation-token

**Infrastructure changes:**
- Added `IAsyncEnumerable` to `SystemCollectionsGeneric` builtins
- Integrated into `emitter.tsx` via `<CollectionResultFiles client={c} options={options} />`
- 7 passing tests in `test/collection-results.test.ts`

**Unblocks:** 4.2.1 (next-link paging), 4.3.1 (continuation-token paging), 4.4.1 (paging client methods)

## 2026-03-02 ŌĆö Task 4.2.1: Implement next-link paging strategy (complete)

**What was done:**
- Modified `src/components/collection-results/CollectionResultFile.tsx` to support next-link paging strategy
- When `pagingMetadata.nextLinkSegments` is present, the component now generates a while(true) loop in GetRawPages:
  1. Sends initial request via Create{Op}Request
  2. Yields each ClientResult page
  3. Extracts next-link URI from response body via cast ((ResponseType)result).PropertyPath
  4. Checks if URI is null (yield break to terminate)
  5. Creates next request via CreateNext{Op}Request(nextPageUri, _options)
- GetContinuationToken now extracts URI and returns ContinuationToken.FromBytes(BinaryData.FromString(uri))

**Key implementation details:**
- Extracted `responseTypeExpr` earlier in the component (needed for both next-link AND convenience methods)
- `buildNextLinkPropertyPath()` handles nested segments with `?.` operator (e.g., "Nested?.NextLink")
- `buildNextLinkGetRawPagesBody()` generates the while-loop with sync/async variants
- `buildNextLinkGetContinuationTokenBody()` generates URI extraction + ContinuationToken creation
- `buildSinglePageGetRawPagesBody()` extracted from the existing inline code for clarity

**Gotcha discovered:**
- The `code` template tag strips leading whitespace when the first template chunk is whitespace-only
  (e.g., `code\`    ${ref}...\`` loses the 4-space indent). Fix: separate indent into a plain string
  child: `"    ", code\`${ref}...\``

**Test additions:**
- 4 new tests in test/collection-results.test.ts for next-link paging
- Tests verify: while loop, initial request, URI extraction, null check, next request, async variant, GetContinuationToken, convenience variant

**Unblocks:** Tasks 4.3.1 (continuation-token paging), 4.4.1 (paging client methods)

## 2026-03-02 ŌĆö Task 2.3.12: Implement additional binary data capture (complete)

### What was done
- Created `src/components/serialization/AdditionalBinaryDataRead.tsx` ŌĆö a new component that generates the catch-all block in the deserialization foreach loop for unknown JSON properties.
- Updated `src/emitter.tsx` to pass `<AdditionalBinaryDataRead />` as children to `<PropertyMatchingLoop>`, filling the children slot that was designed for this purpose.
- Generated pattern: `if (options.Format != "W") { additionalBinaryDataProperties.Add(prop.Name, BinaryData.FromString(prop.Value.GetRawText())); }`

### Bug fixes (pre-existing failures resolved)
1. **XML-only models incorrectly implementing IJsonModel** ŌĆö Added `UsageFlags.Json` check in `emitter.tsx` to conditionally render JSON-specific components (JsonModelInterfaceWrite, JsonModelWriteCore, JsonModelInterfaceCreate, JsonModelCreateCore, JsonDeserialize, DeserializationConstructor) only when the model supports JSON. XML-only models now correctly implement only `IPersistableModel<T>`.
2. **Nested dictionary WriteStartObject count** ŌĆö Corrected test expectation from 2 to 3 in `test/model-serialization.test.ts`. The correct count is 3: 1 from IJsonModel<T>.Write() + 2 from the nested Record<Record<string>> property.
3. **Preprocessor directive newline issue in AdditionalBinaryDataWrite** ŌĆö Fixed `src/components/serialization/AdditionalBinaryDataWrite.tsx` where `\n` inside `code` template literals was not rendering as newlines. Separated newlines into plain strings, keeping `code` templates only for refkey resolution.

### Key design decision
Created a dedicated `AdditionalBinaryDataRead` component (mirroring the existing `AdditionalBinaryDataWrite`) rather than building the catch-all directly into PropertyMatchingLoop. This follows the existing architecture pattern and uses the children slot that was explicitly designed for this purpose.

### Tests added
- 3 new tests in `test/model-serialization.test.ts` under `describe("AdditionalBinaryDataRead")`:
  1. "captures unknown properties with format guard" ŌĆö verifies `options.Format != "W"` guard and `additionalBinaryDataProperties.Add(...)` call
  2. "appears after all known property matches" ŌĆö verifies ordering (catch-all after all `prop.NameEquals` checks)
  3. "uses BinaryData.FromString for raw text preservation" ŌĆö verifies the `BinaryData.FromString(prop.Value.GetRawText())` pattern

### Remaining failures
- 4 smoke test failures remain ŌĆö caused by missing infrastructure files (task 5.1.5: ClientUriBuilder, ModelSerializationExtensions, CancellationTokenExtensions, ClientPipelineExtensions). NOT related to model serialization.

### Pattern learned
- The `code` tagged template from `@alloy-js/core` does NOT properly render `\n` escape sequences inside the template literal. Always separate newlines into plain strings (`{"\n    "}`) and keep `code` templates for refkey interpolation only.

## 2026-03-02 ŌĆö Task 5.1.5: Split into 4 sub-tasks

### What was done
Split task 5.1.5 "Generate remaining infrastructure files" (10 files) into 4 manageable sub-tasks:

- Updated downstream dependencies: 5.1.6 depends on all 4 sub-tasks, 9.1.1 depends on 5.1.5d specifically

### Pattern for next iterations
Follow the ArgumentFile.tsx pattern for all infrastructure files:
```tsx
export function XFile(props: { packageName: string; options: EmitterOptions }) {
  return (
    <SourceFile path="src/Generated/Internal/X.cs" using={[...]}>
      {getLicenseHeader(props.options)}
      <Namespace name={props.packageName}>
        <ClassDeclaration internal static partial name="X">
          {code`... method body ...`}
        </ClassDeclaration>
      </Namespace>
    </SourceFile>
  );
}
```

- Added `buildCreateRequestArgs` helper to construct Create{Op}Request args, replacing token with nextToken on subsequent iterations
- Renamed `buildNextLinkPropertyPath` to `buildResponsePropertyPath` (generic, reusable for both next-link and continuation-token)
- Updated `buildConstructorDoc` to accept operation params and generate `<param>` docs for each

Added 6 tests in `test/collection-results.test.ts`:
1. Body-based continuation-token sync protocol GetRawPages loop
2. Body-based continuation-token async protocol GetRawPagesAsync loop

**Key finding:**
- The Alloy constructor formatter wraps parameters to multiple lines when the class name + parameters exceed a line length threshold. The `CollectionResultOfT` variant with 3 constructor params crosses this threshold and uses multi-line format, while the non-OfT variant with the same params stays on one line. This is due to the longer class name.

## Task 4.5.1 ŌĆö Implement LRO method signatures and return types (2026-03-03)

### What was done
- Analyzed LRO (Long-Running Operation) method generation pipeline
- Confirmed that for System.ClientModel (non-Azure), LRO methods use identical signatures and return types as basic methods (ClientResult/ClientResult<T>)
- Updated ProtocolMethod.tsx and ConvenienceMethod.tsx filters to explicitly exclude "lropaging" (kind that needs separate handling in task 4.5.2)
- Added `@azure-tools/typespec-client-generator-core` to the test host libraries to enable `@markAsLro` decorator in tests
- Created comprehensive LRO test suite (6 tests): protocol methods, convenience methods, path+body params, model return, CreateRequest, XML docs
- All 898 tests pass (6 new)

### Design decision
LRO methods share the same generation pipeline as basic methods. No separate LRO component is needed because:
- In System.ClientModel, LRO method signatures are identical to basic methods
- LRO metadata (finalStateVia, finalResponse, resultPath) doesn't affect method signatures in the non-Azure target
- The existing filter `m.kind !== "paging"` already passes LRO methods through correctly
- The `lropaging` kind is excluded from basic/LRO filters (needs combined handling in 4.5.2)

### Patterns used
- `@markAsLro` from `Azure.ClientGenerator.Core.Legacy` to force TCGC to produce kind "lro" in tests
- Multi-line assertion pattern for async convenience methods (printWidth causes wrapping)
- Used short type names (Job, Status, Result) to keep signatures within printWidth

### Things the next person should know
- `@markAsLro` only works on operations that return a model (void returns produce a warning and are ignored)
- TCGC's `SdkServiceMethod` union includes both `SdkLroServiceMethod` (kind "lro") and `SdkLroPagingServiceMethod` (kind "lropaging")
- The "lropaging" kind is now excluded from both protocol and convenience method filters ŌĆö task 4.5.2 will handle this combined case
- The RestClient (CreateRequest methods) already handles all HTTP operations uniformly, including LRO

## 2026-03-03 ŌĆö Task 9.1.2: Implement multipart request building

Changes made:
- Modified `src/components/clients/ProtocolMethod.tsx`:
  - Added `SdkBodyParameter` import
  - Added `isMultipartFormData()` helper function
  - In `buildProtocolParams()`, added synthetic `contentType: string` parameter
    immediately after body parameter for multipart/form-data operations
  - Priority is body+1 to ensure it appears right after `content` param
  - Marked as required string (isStringType: true) for proper validation

- Modified `src/components/clients/RestClientFile.tsx`:
  - Added `isMultipartFormData()` helper function
  - In `buildMethodParams()`, added `contentType: string` parameter for multipart
  - In `buildRequestBody()`, changed Content-Type header to use `contentType`
    variable (not hardcoded string) when operation is multipart/form-data

- Created `test/multipart-request-building.test.ts` with 8 tests covering:
  - Protocol method has contentType parameter for multipart ops
  - contentType validated with AssertNotNullOrEmpty
  - XML docs include contentType parameter
  - CreateRequest method has contentType parameter
  - CreateRequest uses contentType variable (not hardcoded string) for Content-Type
  - Non-multipart operations are not affected (regression test)
  - Protocol method passes contentType to CreateRequest
  - CreateRequest sets request.Content for multipart body

Design decision: Added synthetic `contentType` parameter matching legacy emitter's
`ScmKnownParameters.ContentType` pattern, rather than letting the Content-Type
header parameter through. This matches the generated output in Spector golden files
exactly: `Basic(BinaryContent content, string contentType, RequestOptions options)`.

Key insight: For multipart, Content-Type must be dynamic because it includes the
boundary string (e.g., "multipart/form-data; boundary=abc123"). The boundary is
generated at runtime by MultiPartFormDataBinaryContent.

All 928 tests pass (8 new).

## 2026-03-03 ŌĆö Task 9.1.3: Write multipart tests (complete)

### What was done
Created `test/multipart.test.ts` with 10 integration tests covering end-to-end multipart generation scenarios:

- **Multiple multipart operations** ŌĆö all ops get `(BinaryContent content, string contentType, RequestOptions options)` signature
- **Mixed client (multipart + non-multipart)** ŌĆö only multipart ops get contentType parameter
- **Infrastructure file for mixed client** ŌĆö MultiPartFormDataBinaryContent generated when at least one multipart op exists
- **Mixed RestClient CreateRequest** ŌĆö multipart uses dynamic contentType, non-multipart uses hardcoded Content-Type
- **Sub-client multipart operations** ŌĆö sub-client ops get contentType parameter via interface pattern
- **Infrastructure file for sub-client-only multipart** ŌĆö file generated even when only sub-client has multipart
- **ContentType validation per operation** ŌĆö AssertNotNullOrEmpty applied to each multipart op independently
- **ContentType passthrough to CreateRequest** ŌĆö each protocol method passes contentType to its CreateRequest
- **Multiple CreateRequest methods** ŌĆö RestClient generates separate CreateRequest for each multipart op
- **Body part count transparency** ŌĆö different multipart body shapes produce same protocol method signature

### Bug fixed
Fixed `detectMultipartOperations()` in `HttpClientCSharpOutput.tsx` ŌĆö it only scanned root clients (`sdkPackage.clients`) but missed sub-client methods in `client.children`. Updated to use `getAllClients()` which does BFS traversal. Without this fix, `MultiPartFormDataBinaryContent.cs` was not generated when only a sub-client had multipart operations.

### Testing notes
- Async method signatures wrap across multiple lines in generated C# ŌĆö use fragment matching (e.g., `toContain("public virtual async Task<ClientResult> UploadAsync(")`) instead of full signature matching
- All 938 tests pass (928 baseline + 10 new), build and lint clean

## 2026-03-03 ŌĆö Task 5.4.2: Implement unreferenced type handling (complete)

Created `src/utils/unreferenced-types.ts` with type reachability analysis:
- `extractModelOrEnumTypes(type)` ŌĆö unwraps container types (arrays, dicts, nullables, unions) to extract leaf model/enum types
- `getDirectReferences(model)` ŌĆö collects immediate type references from a model (properties, base model, discriminated subtypes, additional properties)
- `collectRootTypes(clients)` ŌĆö extracts all model/enum types from operation signatures (method params, responses, exceptions) AND operation-level responses/exceptions
- `findReachableTypes(roots)` ŌĆö BFS from root types through the reference graph
- `applyUnreferencedTypeHandling(models, enums, clients, option)` ŌĆö main entry point that applies the option

Updated `src/options.ts`:
- Added `"unreferenced-types-handling": "removeOrInternalize"` to defaultOptions

Updated `src/emitter.tsx`:
- Calls `applyUnreferencedTypeHandling()` before passing types to components
- Moved `clients` extraction before models/enums to pass to the handler

Key learnings:
- For paging methods, `method.response.type` is the ITEM type (e.g., `Thing`), not the page wrapper type (e.g., `PageThing`). Must also collect types from `method.operation.responses` to get page wrapper models.
- `SdkMethod` in current TCGC version equals `SdkServiceMethod` ŌĆö no `SdkClientAccessor` kind exists. All methods have `parameters`, `response`, and `operation`.
- TCGC already filters sdkPackage.models to types reachable from operations, so in practice the unreferenced-types-handling mainly serves as a safety net. But the implementation correctly handles cases where types might be unreachable.
- Tests use mock TCGC types (not full TypeSpec compilation) for unit testing the reference graph logic.

## Task 7.1.1: Implement dynamic model structure ŌĆö 2026-03-03

### What was done
- Created `src/builtins/system-component-model.ts` with `EditorBrowsableAttribute` and `EditorBrowsableState` library declarations
- Created `src/builtins/system-text-json-serialization.ts` with `JsonIgnoreAttribute` library declaration
- Updated `src/builtins/index.ts` to export new builtins
- Created `src/components/models/DynamicModel.tsx` with:
  - `isDynamicModel()` function ŌĆö detects `UsageFlags.JsonMergePatch` on models
  - `DynamicModelMembers` component ŌĆö generates `_patch` field and `Patch` ref-return property
- Modified `src/components/models/ModelFile.tsx` to conditionally render `DynamicModelMembers` for models with `JsonMergePatch` usage flag
- Created `test/dynamic-model.test.ts` with 5 tests covering field generation, property attributes, pragma warnings, using directives, and regression for non-dynamic models

### Design decisions
- **Approach**: Created separate `DynamicModel.tsx` component rather than inlining into `ModelFile.tsx` for separation of concerns
- **`_additionalBinaryDataProperties` kept alongside `_patch`**: The serialization code (task 7.2.1) still references `_additionalBinaryDataProperties`. Removing it now would break compilation. Task 7.2.1 should replace it with `_patch` in the serialization path.
- **Constructor change deferred**: The "internal constructor accepts JsonPatch" acceptance criterion is deferred to task 7.2.1, which updates the serialization constructor to use `in JsonPatch patch` instead of `additionalBinaryDataProperties`.
- **`[Experimental("SCME0001")]` attribute deferred**: `ExperimentalAttribute` is inaccessible (internal) on `netstandard2.0` from `System.ClientModel` v1.9.0. The attribute will be added in task 7.2.1 with `#if NET8_0_OR_GREATER` conditional compilation. For now, `#pragma warning disable SCME0001` suppresses the experimental diagnostic from the `JsonPatch` type itself.

### Patterns used
- `Attribute` component from `@alloy-js/csharp` for `[JsonIgnore]` and `[EditorBrowsable(Never)]`
- `Field` component for the `_patch` field declaration
- `code` template for the `ref` return property (Property component doesn't support ref returns or expression bodies)
- `createLibrary()` for new builtin type declarations (auto-generates `using` directives)

### What next person should know
- Task 7.2.1 should: (1) replace `_additionalBinaryDataProperties` with `_patch` in the serialization constructor, (2) add `[Experimental("SCME0001")]` with conditional compilation, (3) update serialization code to use `_patch` for patch-aware serialization
- The `Attribute` component strips the `Attribute` suffix from type names (e.g., `JsonIgnoreAttribute` ŌåÆ `[JsonIgnore]`)
- The `Property` component from `@alloy-js/csharp` does NOT support `ref` return types or expression bodies ŌĆö use `code` template for these
- The `Field` component does NOT support `attributes` prop ŌĆö use standalone `<Attribute>` above the `<Field>` to add attributes

## Task 7.2.1: Implement patch-aware serialization ŌĆö 2026-03-03

**What was done:**
- Created `src/components/serialization/DynamicPropertySerializer.tsx` with `DynamicWritePropertySerialization` component that generates patch-aware property serialization for dynamic (JSON Merge Patch) models
- Modified `src/components/serialization/JsonModelInterfaceWrite.tsx` to add root-level `Patch.Contains("$"u8)` check in `IJsonModel.Write` for dynamic models, with SCME0001 pragma wrapping
- Modified `src/components/serialization/JsonModelWriteCore.tsx` to use `DynamicWritePropertySerialization` for dynamic models, add `#pragma warning disable/restore SCME0001` wrapping, and `Patch.WriteTo(writer)` at end
- Modified `src/components/serialization/ModelSerializationFile.tsx` to add `using System.Text;` import for dynamic models
- Modified `src/emitter.tsx` to skip `AdditionalBinaryDataWrite` for dynamic models (replaced by `Patch.WriteTo`)
- Created `src/builtins/system-text.ts` with `Encoding` library declaration for `System.Text` namespace
- Updated `src/builtins/index.ts` and `src/components/serialization/index.ts` with new exports
- Created `test/dynamic-model-serialization.test.ts` with 9 tests covering: root patch check, required property wrapping, optional property guard, Patch.WriteTo, no additionalBinaryData, regression for non-dynamic, model property, SCME0001 pragma, using System.Text import

**Serialization patterns implemented:**
- Simple required properties: `if (!Patch.Contains("$.name"u8)) { write }`
- Optional properties: `if (guard && !Patch.Contains("$.name"u8)) { write }`
- Required nullable: `!Patch.Contains` wrapper + `else { WriteNull }`
- Model properties: `!Patch.Contains` wrapper with `WriteObjectValue`
- Lists/Arrays: Two-branch pattern (Patch.Contains ŌåÆ raw value, else ŌåÆ `for` loop with per-element `Patch.IsRemoved` checks)
- Dictionaries: `!Patch.Contains` wrapper + per-key `patchContains` checks with `#if NET8_0_OR_GREATER` `Span<byte>` stackalloc optimization
- Nested collections: Recursive support for list-of-list, dict-of-dict, list-of-dict, dict-of-list
- `Patch.WriteTo(writer, path)` after each collection serialization

**Key design decisions:**
- Created separate `DynamicPropertySerializer.tsx` using string-based helpers (not JSX) to avoid Alloy Babel plugin issues with deeply nested JSX fragments
- The `using System.Text;` import is handled via `SourceFile`'s `using` prop in `ModelSerializationFile.tsx` instead of via refkey references
- Reuses exported helpers from `PropertySerializer.tsx` (getWriteMethodInfo, buildGuardCondition, etc.)
- Dynamic model items in lists use `element.Patch.IsRemoved("$"u8)`, primitive items use `Patch.IsRemoved(Encoding.UTF8.GetBytes(path))`

**Known limitations:**
- BinaryData/unknown type properties are not yet handled in serialization (pre-existing gap)
- Deserialization changes (data parameter, JsonPatch construction, constructor changes) are separate from this task

## 2026-03-03 ŌĆö Task 10.1.4: Validate parameter scenarios (complete)

**Key differences identified vs Spector golden files** (tracked as follow-up tasks):
1. **Collection parameter type** (10.1.4a): Our emitter uses `string[]`; golden uses `IEnumerable<string>`. Protocol methods incorrectly flatten collections to `string`.
2. **Implicit body spread** (10.1.4b): Our emitter wraps implicit body in a synthesized model (e.g., `SimpleRequest`); golden spreads as individual scalar parameters (e.g., `string name`).
3. **Non-versioned ClientOptions**: Known difference ŌĆö uses `ClientPipelineOptions` directly instead of custom `XxxClientOptions`. Already documented.
4. **Namespace underscore prefix**: Known difference ŌĆö `ExplicitBody` vs `_ExplicitBody`. Already documented.

**TypeSpec syntax gotcha**: Collection format decorators use `@query(#{ explode: true })` for multi, `@encode(ArrayEncoding.spaceDelimited)` for SSV, `@encode(ArrayEncoding.pipeDelimited)` for pipes. The old `format` property is deprecated.

  the element type. Dict remains unchanged using TypeExpression.

  `IEnumerable<string>` appears in generated output for `string[]` query parameters.

Pattern: Both fixes mirror RestClientFile.tsx (line 426-431) which already handled arrays
correctly for CreateRequest method signatures. The refkey `SystemCollectionsGeneric.IEnumerable`
auto-generates the `using System.Collections.Generic;` directive.

## 2026-03-03: Task 10.1.5a ŌĆö Fix BinaryData_2 naming conflict in bytes models

### What was done
Fixed the `BinaryData_2` naming conflict that occurred when a model had both a `bytes` property and `_additionalBinaryDataProperties`. The root cause was two separate `createLibrary("System", ...)` calls each defining a `BinaryData` type:
1. `src/builtins/system.ts` ŌĆö used by ModelFile, ModelConstructors, serialization components
2. `src/components/CSharpTypeExpression.tsx` ŌĆö used for scalar type overrides (bytes ŌåÆ BinaryData)

These created two different Alloy refkeys for the same `System.BinaryData` type, causing Alloy's naming policy to disambiguate one as `BinaryData_2`.

### Fix applied
- Removed the duplicate `SystemBinaryData = createLibrary("System", { BinaryData: ... })` from `CSharpTypeExpression.tsx`
- Replaced with import of `System` from `../builtins/system.js` (the canonical source)
- Also removed the alloy-js/csharp built-in System import since our custom System has DateTimeOffset/TimeSpan too
- Updated `index.ts` to remove the `SystemBinaryData` export
- Updated test expectations in `bytes_encoding.md` from `BinaryData_2` ŌåÆ `BinaryData`
- Updated `type-expression.test.tsx` to use `System.BinaryData` instead of `SystemBinaryData.BinaryData`

### Key pattern
Never create duplicate `createLibrary()` calls for the same namespace+type ŌĆö they create distinct refkeys that Alloy disambiguates with `_2` suffixes when both appear in the same file scope.

### Files changed
- `src/components/CSharpTypeExpression.tsx` ŌĆö removed duplicate library, unified imports
- `src/components/index.ts` ŌĆö removed SystemBinaryData export
- `test/type-expression.test.tsx` ŌĆö updated test for new import
- `test/scenarios/encoding/bytes_encoding.md` ŌĆö fixed BinaryData_2 ŌåÆ BinaryData expectations

### Validation
- `pnpm build` Ō£ģ
- `pnpm test` Ō£ģ (1078/1078 tests pass)
- `pnpm lint` Ō£ģ

2026-03-03 ŌĆö Task 10.1.5c: Fix ISO8601 naming preserved as acronym in model names (complete)

Problem: Model name `ISO8601DurationProperty` was incorrectly converted to `Iso8601DurationProperty`
by the C# PascalCase naming policy. `changecase.pascalCase()` breaks consecutive uppercase acronyms.

Fix: Created `createHttpClientNamePolicy()` in `HttpClientCSharpOutput.tsx` that wraps
`createCSharpNamePolicy()`. For type-level contexts (class, struct, enum, interface, record),
names that already start with an uppercase letter are preserved as-is (TCGC provides correct casing).
Names starting with lowercase (e.g., method names being PascalCased) still go through the standard policy.

Key insight: The "class" naming context was used for BOTH type names (already PascalCase from TCGC)
AND method names (camelCase from TCGC needing PascalCase). The heuristic `/^[A-Z]/` distinguishes
these cases ŌĆö type names start with uppercase, method names start with lowercase.

Changes:
- `src/components/HttpClientCSharpOutput.tsx`: Added `createHttpClientNamePolicy()` function and
  `typeContexts` set. Changed `namePolicy` prop from `createCSharpNamePolicy()` to
  `createHttpClientNamePolicy()`.
- `test/scenarios/encoding/duration_encoding.md`: Updated scenario test expectations from
  `Iso8601DurationProperty` to `ISO8601DurationProperty`
- `test/model.test.ts`: Added "preserves acronyms in model names (ISO8601)" test

Tests: 1079 passed (1 new), 0 failed. Build and lint clean.

## 2026-03-03 ŌĆö Task 10.1.7: Validate versioning scenarios (complete)

**Problem:** No scenario tests existed for versioning scenarios (added/removed). Additionally, multi-type named unions (e.g., `union Foo { string, int32 }`) produced `<Unresolved Symbol>` instead of `BinaryData`.

**Fix 1 ŌĆö Multi-type named union ŌåÆ BinaryData:** Added `isMultiTypeNamedUnion()` helper to `CSharpTypeExpression.tsx`. When a named union has variants with different root scalar types (e.g., string + numeric), it's mapped to `BinaryData` instead of delegating to the default TypeExpression (which can't resolve it). The helper:
- Filters out null/void variants
- Detects non-scalar/non-literal variants as multi-type
- For scalar variants, walks the `.baseScalar` chain to compare root types
- Returns true when root types differ (e.g., "string" vs "numeric")

**Fix 2 ŌĆö Versioning scenario tests:** Created two scenario markdown files:
- `test/scenarios/versioning/versioning_added.md` ŌĆö validates @added decorator behavior with 6 code blocks (ModelV1, ModelV2, EnumV1, EnumV2, AddedClient, InterfaceV2)
- `test/scenarios/versioning/versioning_removed.md` ŌĆö validates @removed decorator behavior with 5 code blocks (ModelV2, ModelV3, EnumV2, EnumV3, RemovedClient)

Both scenarios verified against Spector golden files in `submodules/typespec/packages/http-client-csharp/generator/TestProjects/Spector/http/versioning/`. All public API signatures match exactly.

**Fix 3 ŌĆö Unit tests:** Added 2 type expression tests:
- "maps multi-type named union to BinaryData" ŌĆö tests `union { string, int32 }`
- "maps named union with derived scalars to BinaryData" ŌĆö tests `union { string, V2Scalar extends int32 }`

**Changes:**
- `src/components/CSharpTypeExpression.tsx`: Added `isMultiTypeNamedUnion()` function and updated Union override
- `test/type-expression.test.tsx`: Added 2 union type override tests
- `test/scenarios/versioning/versioning_added.md`: New scenario test

## 2026-03-03 ŌĆö Task 10.1.6.1: Fix optional int32 mapping for @pageSize parameter

**What was done:**
- Fixed optional value type parameters (int, bool, float, etc.) to render as nullable (`int?`, `bool?`) in C# method signatures
- The fix applies to protocol methods, convenience methods, paging methods, and RestClient CreateRequest methods

**Files modified:**
- `src/utils/nullable.ts` ŌĆö Added `isProtocolParamValueType()` and `isConvenienceParamValueType()` helpers
- `src/components/clients/ProtocolMethod.tsx` ŌĆö Added `maybeNullable()` helper, used in `buildProtocolParams`
- `src/components/clients/ConvenienceMethod.tsx` ŌĆö Added `maybeNullable()` helper, used in `buildConvenienceParams`
- `src/components/clients/RestClientFile.tsx` ŌĆö Added `maybeNullable()` helper, used in `buildMethodParams`
- Updated test expectations in convenience-method.test.ts, rest-client.test.ts, and page_size_paging.md

**Patterns used:**
- `maybeNullable(typeExpr, sdkType, optional)` ŌĆö appends `?` to value type expressions when optional
- `isProtocolParamValueType(type)` ŌĆö checks if type maps to C# value type (unwraps enums to wire types)
- `isConvenienceParamValueType(type)` ŌĆö same but enums are always value types in convenience context

**Key learning:**
- Protocol methods unwrap enums to wire types, so string-backed enum ŌåÆ string (reference type, no `?`), int-backed enum ŌåÆ int (value type, gets `?`)
- Convenience methods keep enums as-is, and enums are value types in C#
- The type expression modification in buildParams propagates to all consumers: method signatures, CollectionResult fields/constructors, and RestClient CreateRequest params

## Task 12.1.1: Fix emitter crash on UnionVariant type in type/property/value-types
**Date**: 2026-03-04

### What was done
Two-part fix for the "Unsupported type for TypeExpression: UnionVariant" crash:

1. **Added `UnionVariant` override in CSharpTypeExpression.tsx** (lines 213-225):
   - Added `.forTypeKind("UnionVariant", ...)` to the Experimental_ComponentOverrides config
   - For variants from named unions (e.g., `ExtendedEnum.EnumValue2`), references the parent union type via `efCsharpRefkey(variant.union)`
   - For unnamed union variants, falls back to `<TypeExpression type={variant.type} />`
   - Imported `UnionVariant` from `@typespec/compiler` and `TypeExpression` from `@typespec/emitter-framework/csharp`

2. **Added `SdkEnumValueType` handling in unreferenced-types.ts** (line 44-45):
   - Added `case "enumvalue": return [type.enumType]` to `extractModelOrEnumTypes()`
   - Without this, parent enum types referenced only through union variants were filtered out as unreachable, leaving unresolved refkey symbols

### Test added
- `test/type-expression.test.tsx`: "maps named union variant to parent union type"
  - Compiles TypeSpec with `union ExtendedEnum { string, EnumValue2: "value2" }` and property `ExtendedEnum.EnumValue2`
  - Verifies emitter produces no diagnostics, model file contains `ExtendedEnum`, no unresolved symbols

### Key insight
The crash had two root causes: (1) TypeExpression didn't handle `UnionVariant` type kind, and (2) the type reachability graph didn't follow `SdkEnumValueType ŌåÆ enumType` edges, so parent enums weren't generated. Both fixes were required.

### Result
1162 tests pass (1 new), 128 skipped, 62 test files. Build and lint clean.

## 2026-03-04: Task 12.2.5 ŌĆö Fix unresolved refkey symbols in union type deserialization (complete)

**What was done:** Fixed `CSharpTypeExpression.tsx` to correctly map all multi-type unions to `BinaryData`, not just named ones. The root cause was `isMultiTypeNamedUnion` rejecting unnamed unions (`if (!union.name) return false`), causing TypeSpec aliases (`MixedTypesUnion = Cat | "a" | int32 | boolean`), mixed literals (`"a" | 2 | 3.3 | true`), inline unions (`string | string[]`), and model unions (`Cat | Dog`) to fall through to `efCsharpRefkey()` which created unresolved references.

**Changes:**
1. **Renamed `isMultiTypeNamedUnion` ŌåÆ `isMultiTypeUnion`** ŌĆö removed the name check so both named and unnamed unions are evaluated.
2. **Added `getVariantBaseKind` helper** ŌĆö categorizes each variant type into "string", "numeric", "boolean", or its own kind. This correctly handles mixed literals (String + Number + Boolean kinds).
3. **Added non-extensible-enum check** ŌĆö if all variants share the same base kind but that kind is NOT a scalar/literal category (e.g., `Cat | Dog` ŌåÆ both "Model"), it's still multi-type ŌåÆ BinaryData.
4. **Reordered override logic** ŌĆö nullable unions checked first (delegated to default), then multi-type (ŌåÆ BinaryData), then named extensible enums (ŌåÆ default), then unnamed extensible enums (ŌåÆ efCsharpRefkey).

**Tests added:** 5 new tests in `test/type-expression.test.tsx`:
- "maps unnamed multi-type alias union to BinaryData" (Cat | "a" | int32 | boolean alias)
- "maps mixed literal type union to BinaryData" ("a" | 2 | 3.3 | true)
- "maps inline scalar+array union to BinaryData" (string | string[])
- "does not map single-type literal union to BinaryData" ("red" | "blue" | "green")
- "maps model-only union to BinaryData" (Cat | Dog)

**Impact:** Fixed all unresolved refkey symbols in type/union spec: MixedTypesCases, MixedLiteralsCases, StringAndArrayCases, GetResponse5, SendRequest5, and the ModelFactory. Went from 65 unresolved symbols to 0 (excluding stale file from old naming).

**Result:** 1168 tests pass (5 new), 128 skipped, 62 test files. Build and lint clean.

## 2026-03-04: Task 12.2.13 ŌĆö Fix CodeGen attribute files using directive ordering (complete)

### What was done
Fixed all four CodeGen attribute files (CodeGenTypeAttribute, CodeGenMemberAttribute, CodeGenSuppressAttribute, CodeGenSerializationAttribute) to place `using System;` after the `#nullable disable` directive instead of before the license header.

### Root cause
Alloy's `<SourceFile>` `using` prop renders using directives at the very top of the file, before any content including the license header. This is documented as gotcha #8 in knowledge.md.

### Fix
Removed `using={["System"]}` prop from all four `<SourceFile>` components in `CodeGenAttributeFiles.tsx` and manually placed `"using System;\n\n"` in the content after the header string. This ensures the ordering matches the legacy emitter: license header ŌåÆ `#nullable disable` ŌåÆ `using System;` ŌåÆ namespace.

### Tests added
4 new tests in `codegen-attributes.test.ts` verifying that `using System;` appears after `#nullable disable` for all four attribute files.

### Patterns used
- Manual using directive placement to work around Alloy SourceFile using-ordering behavior
- Same pattern should be applied to other infrastructure files if their using ordering needs fixing

### For next iterations
- Other infrastructure files (Argument.cs, Optional.cs, etc.) have the same using-ordering issue but that's tracked separately
- The namespace brace style (Egyptian vs Allman) is a different issue controlled by Alloy's renderer, not by individual components

## 2026-03-04: Task 12.2.3 ŌĆö Fix multiline XML documentation comments (complete)

### What was done
Created `src/utils/doc.ts` with a `formatDocLines()` utility that replaces `\n` with `\n/// ` in documentation text before interpolation into XML doc comment strings. Applied it in three files:
- `src/components/clients/ProtocolMethod.tsx` ŌĆö description and param doc lines in `buildXmlDoc()`
- `src/components/clients/ConvenienceMethod.tsx` ŌĆö summary and param doc lines in `buildConvenienceXmlDoc()`
- `src/components/clients/ClientFile.tsx` ŌĆö client class summary and constructor param docs

### Root cause
When TypeSpec `@doc` decorators contain multiline text (using triple-quoted strings `"""..."""`), the raw text includes newlines. Interpolating this into `/// <tag>` strings produced continuation lines without the `///` prefix, breaking C# syntax (e.g., `/// <param name="x"> first line\nsecond line </param>`).

### Tests added
- `test/doc-utils.test.ts` ŌĆö 6 unit tests for `formatDocLines()` covering single-line, multiline, empty, trailing newline, param context, summary context
- `test/convenience-method.test.ts` ŌĆö 1 integration test for multiline @doc on parameters
- `test/protocol-method.test.ts` ŌĆö 1 integration test for multiline @doc on parameters  
- `test/client-file.test.ts` ŌĆö 1 integration test for multiline @doc on service summary

### Patterns used
- String sanitization utility in `src/utils/doc.ts` ŌĆö preferred over switching to Alloy DocComment components per knowledge.md guidance that raw strings are preferred for doc comments
- Applied at all interpolation points where doc content flows from TypeSpec into `///` comment strings

### For next iterations
- TypeSpec multiline strings use triple-quoted syntax (`"""..."""`) ŌĆö use this in tests, not `\n`
- All test TypeSpec snippets need `using TypeSpec.Http;` and `@service namespace` for HttpTester
- If new doc comment generation points are added, import and use `formatDocLines` from `../../utils/doc.js`

**Result:** 1183 tests pass (9 new), 128 skipped, 63 test files. Build and lint clean.

## 2026-03-04 ŌĆö Task 12.2.6: Fix missing sub-client classes for deeply nested route operations

- Updated `src/components/clients/ClientFile.tsx`, `RestClientFile.tsx`, and `CollectionResultFile.tsx` to use `getClientFileName()` for SourceFile path generation instead of just the short class name

- For single-level hierarchies (root > child), the result equals the short name, so no existing tests break

- The legacy emitter uses concatenated hierarchical names for all sub-client files
- TypeSpec uses `namespace` (not `interface`) for deeply nested operation groups
- Class names remain short (e.g., `class Standard`) with namespaces handling disambiguation; only filenames use the concatenated form

## 2026-03-04: Task 12.2.13 ŌĆö Fix sub-client class/namespace naming conflict

**Problem**: Sub-client classes (e.g., `Model`, `Alias`) conflict with their own namespace in C#. `namespace Parameters.Spread.Model { class Model }` causes CS0118 errors.

**Solution**: Added namespace cleaning utilities to `src/utils/package-name.ts`:
- `collectInvalidNamespaceSegments()` ŌĆö detects client names matching last namespace segment, plus static reserved words (Type, Array, Enum)
- `cleanNamespace()` ŌĆö prefixes invalid segments with `_` (e.g., `Parameters.Spread.Model` ŌåÆ `Parameters.Spread._Model`)
- `cleanAllNamespaces()` ŌĆö applies cleaning to all clients, models, and enums in place

Called `cleanAllNamespaces()` from `emitter.tsx` after `ensureModelNamespaces()`, consistent with existing namespace mutation pattern.

**Pattern**: Centralized pre-render mutation (same approach as `ensureModelNamespaces`). This avoids changing every component that uses `.namespace`.

**Files changed**: `src/utils/package-name.ts`, `src/emitter.tsx`, `test/package-name.test.ts`

## 2026-03-04: Task 12.2.10 ŌĆö Fix union float/int literal property types in optionality spec

**Problem**: TCGC preserves numeric literal union values verbatim as enum member names (e.g., "1.25", "2.375"). The Alloy `pascalCase` transform from `change-case` converts "1.25" ŌåÆ "1_25" (word at index>0 starting with digit gets `_` prefix, but at the wrong position), and "1" ŌåÆ "1" (unchanged). Both are invalid C# identifiers.

**Root cause**: `change-case` v5's `pascalCaseTransformFactory` adds `_` before digits only at word index > 0: `"1_25"` comes from words `["1", "25"]` where the second word gets `_` prefix. The legacy emitter's `ToIdentifierName()` instead prefixes the WHOLE result with `_` and removes non-alphanumeric chars.

**Solution**: Added `fixedEnumMemberName()` utility function exported from `FixedEnumFile.tsx`:
- If `rawName` starts with a digit: `_${rawName.replace(/[^a-zA-Z0-9]/g, "")}`
  - "1.25" ŌåÆ "_125", "2.375" ŌåÆ "_2375", "1" ŌåÆ "_1"
- Otherwise: delegates to `namePolicy.getName(rawName, "enum-member")`

Also removed `<EnumMember>` component and replaced with raw text output, since:
- `EnumMember` internally applies `pascalCase` which can't produce `_125`
- No refkeys to fixed enum members exist anywhere else in the codebase

**Files changed**: `src/components/enums/FixedEnumFile.tsx`, `src/components/enums/FixedEnumSerializationFile.tsx`, `test/fixed-enum.test.ts`, `test/fixed-enum-serialization.test.ts`

**Tests added**: 2 new tests for numeric-starting enum member names in declaration and serialization files.
**All 65 test files pass (1227 passed, 128 skipped)**

## Task 12.2.11 ŌĆö Fix pageable collection result types with long names (2026-03-04)

### What was done
Fixed two bugs in `CollectionResultFile.tsx`:

1. **Class name mismatch**: CollectionResultFile used `getClientFileName()` (full parent hierarchy like
   `ServerDrivenPaginationContinuationToken`) while PagingMethods used `namePolicy.getName(client.name, "class")`
   (immediate name like `ContinuationToken`). The `new` instantiation in PagingMethods didn't match the
   class name in CollectionResultFile. Fixed by aligning CollectionResultFile to use immediate client name.

2. **ContinuationToken type conflict**: When a client is named `ContinuationToken`, C# resolves the
   unqualified `ContinuationToken` to the client class instead of `System.ClientModel.ContinuationToken`.
   This causes compile errors in `GetContinuationToken()` return type and `ContinuationToken.FromBytes()`
   static calls. Fixed by detecting the naming conflict and using `global::System.ClientModel.ContinuationToken`.

### Files modified
- `src/components/collection-results/CollectionResultFile.tsx` ŌĆö shorter class names, FQN for ContinuationToken
- `test/scenarios/paging/continuation_token_params.md` ŌĆö updated expectations for FQN
- `test/collection-results.test.ts` ŌĆö added 2 tests for ContinuationToken conflict detection

### Patterns
- When a C# client class name collides with an SCM type name, use `global::` fully-qualified names
- Collection result class names use immediate client name (matching PagingMethods), not full hierarchy

## Task 13.1 ŌĆö Fix file header ordering: license before using directives (2026-03-04)

### What was done
Fixed the file header ordering so license/auto-generated header appears before `using` directives
in all generated C# files. The Alloy C# `SourceFile` component (v0.22.0) renders auto-detected
usings before children content. Since the header was injected as children, it ended up after usings.

**Approach**: Post-processing ŌĆö after Alloy renders the JSX tree, a `reorderFileHeader()` function
detects files where `using` directives precede the header block (auto-generated + nullable disable)
and reorders them. This was chosen over creating a custom SourceFile wrapper because the internal
namespace scoping mechanisms of `@alloy-js/csharp` (NamespaceScopes, getGlobalNamespace) are not
exported, making it impossible to fully replicate the C# SourceFile's behavior.

### Files created
- `src/utils/reorder-header.ts` ŌĆö reorderFileHeader() and reorderAllFileHeaders() functions
- `test/reorder-header.test.ts` ŌĆö 5 unit tests + 3 integration tests

### Files modified
- `src/emitter.tsx` ŌĆö replaced `writeOutput()` with custom render ŌåÆ reorder ŌåÆ write pipeline

### Design Decision
Rejected approach: Creating a custom CSharpFile component wrapping CoreSourceFile directly.
Reason: The @alloy-js/csharp package (v0.22.0) doesn't export internal symbols needed for proper
namespace scope management (NamespaceScopes, useNamespaceContext, getGlobalNamespace). Without
these, refkey resolution fails because the scope hierarchy is incomplete. The submodule source
has a `header` prop fix but it's not in the published package.

### Patterns
- Post-processing approach allows the fix to work without modifying the Alloy package
- The reorderFileHeader function is idempotent ŌĆö files already in correct order are unchanged
- When @alloy-js/csharp adds the `header` prop support, this post-processing can be removed

## Task 13.2 ŌĆö Fix namespace brace style: Allman (next-line) instead of K&R (same-line) (2026-03-04)

**What was done:**
Fixed namespace brace style in all generated C# files from K&R (`namespace Foo {`) to Allman (`namespace Foo\n{`). The Alloy C# `Namespace` component renders K&R by default. Applied a post-processing step to convert after rendering, matching the pattern established by `reorderFileHeader`.

**Approach:** Post-processing ŌĆö `fixNamespaceBraceStyle()` uses a regex to find `namespace <name> {` on the same line and split into two lines. Uses `[ \t]*` (not `\s*`) to capture only horizontal whitespace, avoiding the bug where `\s*` captures newlines in multiline regex mode causing duplicate blank lines.

**Files created:**
- `src/utils/namespace-brace-style.ts` ŌĆö `fixNamespaceBraceStyle()` and `fixAllNamespaceBraceStyles()` functions
- `test/namespace-brace-style.test.ts` ŌĆö 8 unit tests covering simple, dotted, full-file, idempotent, comment-safe, and class-brace-safe cases

**Files modified:**
- `src/emitter.tsx` ŌĆö added `fixAllNamespaceBraceStyles(tree)` to the post-processing pipeline
- `src/utils/reorder-header.ts` ŌĆö updated docstring example to show Allman style
- `test/scenarios/enums/extensible_enum.md` ŌĆö updated expected output to Allman style

**Key gotcha:** In JavaScript multiline regex, `\s*` matches newlines. When the regex `^(\s*)(namespace...)` is used with the `m` flag, `(\s*)` can capture `\n` from a blank line before the namespace keyword, causing the replacement `$1$2\n$1{` to insert a duplicate blank line. Always use `[ \t]*` for horizontal-whitespace-only matching in multiline regexes.

## 2026-03-04: Task 13.16 ŌĆö Fix RestClient CreateRequest method line breaks
- **Problem**: In `buildRequestBody()` in `RestClientFile.tsx`, statements using the `code` template literal with `\n` at the start had the newline swallowed by the Alloy framework, causing statements to concatenate on the same line (e.g., `uri.AppendPath(...);PipelineMessage message = ...`).
- **Root Cause**: The `code` template tag from `@alloy-js/core` strips/ignores leading `\n` characters, unlike plain strings where `\n` works fine.
- **Fix**: Separated `"\n"` into a standalone plain string pushed before the `code` template literal. Applied to 4 locations: PipelineMessage creation, PipelineRequest extraction, repeatability-request-id header, and repeatability-first-sent header.
- **Pattern**: When using `code` template literals from Alloy with newlines, always push `"\n"` as a separate plain string argument rather than embedding it inside the template literal.
- **Tests**: Added regression assertion in rest-client.test.ts to catch concatenated statements. All 1241 unit tests + 102 scenario tests pass.

## 2026-03-04: Task 13.8 ŌĆö Fix property summary doc trailing period

Added `ensureTrailingPeriod()` utility to `src/utils/doc.ts` and applied it in `ModelProperty.tsx` to ensure all property XML doc summaries end with a period, matching the golden file convention.

**Root cause**: TCGC's `doc`/`summary` fields carry raw TypeSpec text without guaranteed trailing periods, but the legacy emitter's `XmlDocStatement.GetPeriodOrEmpty()` always adds one. The new emitter was passing text through without normalisation.

**Files modified**:

- `test/model.test.ts` ŌĆö 1 new test "adds trailing period to doc comments when source omits it" using TypeSpec `/** text */` without period

**Pattern for future tasks**: The `ensureTrailingPeriod` utility should be applied in any component generating `<summary>` tags from dynamic TCGC content. Other affected files (ClientFile.tsx, ConvenienceMethod.tsx, enum files) have their own tasks (13.3-13.7, 13.24).

## 2026-03-04: Task 13.17 ŌĆö Fix duplicate Accept header in RestClient request methods
- **Problem**: When an operation has both a body (triggering Content-Type) and a response body (triggering Accept), TCGC exposes Accept as a constant header param. The header loop rendered it, and then the auto-derived Accept logic also rendered it ŌĆö producing duplicate `request.Headers.Set("Accept", ...)` lines.
- **Root Cause**: The header loop at line 1043 skipped implicit Content-Type and special headers but did NOT skip constant Accept headers. The auto-derived Accept logic at line 1095 only checked for *variable* Accept params (`!isConstantType(p.type)`), so constant Accept headers fell through both code paths.
- **Fix**: Added `isConstantAcceptHeader()` helper that checks `serializedName === "accept" && isConstantType(param.type)`. Added a `continue` guard in the header loop to skip constant Accept headers, since they're already handled by the auto-derived Accept logic (which ensures correct ordering after Content-Type).
- **Design Decision**: Chose to filter constant Accept from the header loop rather than broadening the `acceptHeaderParam` check, because the auto-derived Accept logic places Accept after Content-Type (matching golden file ordering). If we let the header loop handle it, Accept would appear before Content-Type.
- **Tests**: Added regression test "does not emit duplicate Accept header for POST with body and response" that checks Accept appears exactly once, Content-Type appears exactly once, and Accept comes after Content-Type. All 1248 tests pass.

## 2026-03-04: Task 13.14 ŌĆö Fix constructor access modifier order: private protected (not protected private)

**What was done:** Fixed the C# access modifier ordering for abstract model constructors. The Alloy framework's `getAccessModifier` function iterates modifiers in `["public", "protected", "private", ...]` order, producing `"protected private"` when both flags are set. C# canonical order is `"private protected"`. 

**Changes:**
1. `src/components/models/ModelConstructors.tsx`: 
   - Added `getCSharpAccessModifier()` helper that produces modifiers in C# canonical order (private before protected, matching `"private protected"` and `"protected internal"`)
   - Updated `OverloadConstructor` to use the new helper instead of Alloy's `getAccessModifier`
   - Replaced `<Constructor>` (from Alloy) with `<OverloadConstructor>` in `BaseModelConstructors` since Alloy's Constructor component has the same ordering issue
   - Removed unused `Constructor` and `getAccessModifier` imports; added `AccessModifiers` type import
2. `test/model.test.ts`: Tightened the regex to match only `private protected` (was accepting both orders)
3. `test/scenarios/models/enum_discriminator.md`: Updated Dog and Snake constructor expectations
4. `test/scenarios/models/single_discriminator.md`: Updated Bird constructor expectation

**Pattern used:** Created a local `getCSharpAccessModifier` function that respects C# canonical modifier ordering instead of relying on Alloy's built-in function which has the wrong order for compound modifiers.

**Note for future loops:** The `_additionalBinaryDataProperties` field already uses string `"private protected"` directly (not boolean flags), so it was already correct. Only the constructor modifiers had this issue.

## 2026-03-04 ŌĆö Task 13.13: Fix empty constructor brace style

**What was done:**
- Fixed empty constructor bodies to use multiline Allman-style braces (`{\n}`) instead of single-line `{}`.
- Fixed empty class bodies (e.g., ModelReaderWriterContext) to use block-body style (`{\n}`) instead of file-scoped declaration (`;`).
- Modified `OverloadConstructor` in `src/components/models/ModelConstructors.tsx` to check for empty children and render `"\n{\n}"` directly instead of using `<Block>` (which renders empty content as `{}`).
- Added `fixEmptyClassBody` post-processing function in `src/utils/namespace-brace-style.ts` to convert file-scoped class declarations (ending with `;`) to block-body style.
- Added 6 unit tests for `fixEmptyClassBody` in `test/namespace-brace-style.test.ts`.
- Added 1 integration test for multiline constructor brace style in `test/client-file.test.ts`.
- Added 1 integration test for empty class body style in `test/model-reader-writer-context.test.ts`.
- Updated 28 scenario test files to match the new brace style.

**Key patterns used:**
- `"\n{\n}"` string in JSX to produce Allman-style empty blocks (Alloy handles indentation automatically).
- Post-processing regex to convert `class Foo : Base;` to `class Foo : Base\n{\n}`.
- Same pattern as `fixNamespaceBraceStyle` ŌĆö applied in the same tree-walking pass.

**What next person should know:**
- The `<Block>` component from `@alloy-js/core` renders empty content as `{}` (no whitespace). This is a framework limitation that cannot be changed from the emitter. The workaround is to bypass `<Block>` for empty bodies.
- Empty class body fix uses regex post-processing because `ClassDeclaration` from `@alloy-js/csharp` renders empty classes with `;` instead of `{}`. Cannot be fixed at the component level.
- Pre-existing lint errors exist in `test/fixed-enum.test.ts` and `test/package-name.test.ts` (unrelated to this task).

## 2026-03-04 ŌĆö Task 13.9: Fix @friendlyName namespace mapping (complete)

### What was done
- Added `getCustomNamespace()` utility function to `src/contexts/custom-code-context.ts`
- Modified `ModelFile.tsx` to use custom namespace override when custom code declares a different namespace via `[CodeGenType]`
- Modified `ModelSerializationFile.tsx` with the same namespace override logic
- Added 4 unit tests for `getCustomNamespace()` in `test/custom-code.test.ts`

### Pattern used
When a user writes a custom partial class in a different namespace (e.g., `[CodeGenType("Friend")]` in `SampleTypeSpec.Models.Custom`), both ModelFile and ModelSerializationFile now detect this via `getCustomNamespace()` and use the custom namespace instead of the TCGC default. This ensures generated and custom partial classes merge correctly in C#.

### Design decision
Component-level namespace override was chosen over emitter-level mutation because:
1. Name policy (PascalCase conversion) is needed to match model names against custom code keys
2. Name policy is only available inside Alloy components (via `useCSharpNamePolicy()` hook)
3. Follows existing pattern where components already use `useCustomCode()` for member suppression

2026-03-04 ŌĆö Task 13.10: Fix @clientName support ŌĆö RenamedModel ŌåÆ RenamedModelCustom (complete)
- Added `applyCustomCodeRenames()` function in `src/emitter.tsx` that mutates TCGC model names
  before rendering when custom code declares [CodeGenType("OriginalName")] on a class with
  a different name. This ensures ALL components that derive the C# class name from `type.name`
  automatically produce the correct custom name.
- Approach: Mutate model.name early (before JSX rendering). Since JS objects are by reference,
  ALL references to the model (including from other models' property types) see the updated name.
  Also updates the custom code map to include entry under the new name for downstream lookups.
- Added 6 unit tests in `test/custom-code.test.ts` under `applyCustomCodeRenames` suite.
- No changes needed in 20+ downstream components ŌĆö the early mutation handles everything.
- Pattern: When needing to change a name that many components read, mutate early at the source
  rather than changing every consumer. This is the TCGC mutation pattern.

## 2026-03-04 ŌĆö Task 13.22: Remove extra infrastructure files not in golden output (DONE)

- Internal/BinaryContentHelper.cs
- Internal/PipelineRequestHeadersExtensions.cs
- Internal/Utf8JsonBinaryContent.cs

These files were always generated by the new emitter but never appear in any golden test
project output. The legacy emitter registers them unconditionally but has a post-processing
tree-shaker (PostProcessor.cs) that prunes unreferenced types ŌĆö since no generated client
code references these helpers, they get removed. The new emitter lacks tree-shaking, so the
fix is to stop rendering them.

- src/emitter.tsx: Removed imports and JSX renders for the 3 components

  assertions from the "generates all helper files" test

The component source files (BinaryContentHelperFile.tsx, Utf8JsonBinaryContentFile.tsx,
PipelineRequestHeadersExtensionsFile.tsx) are preserved for future conditional use when
client method body generation is implemented and actually references these helpers.

Design decision: Chose unconditional removal over conditional generation because:
1. No golden output includes these files
2. No current component references them (only emitter.tsx rendered them)
3. Conditional logic would be premature without knowing exact usage triggers

## 2026-03-04 ŌĆö Task 13.12: Fix client constructor pattern ŌĆö separate auth constructors (DONE)

Refactored `RootClientConstructors` in `ClientFile.tsx` to generate separate constructors per auth scheme instead of a single combined constructor. The legacy emitter pattern generates:

1. A short (convenience) constructor for the FIRST auth scheme only (delegates to full with default options)
2. A full constructor per auth scheme, each with its own body: validates only its auth param, assigns only its auth field, creates pipeline with only its auth policy

Key changes:
- **`src/components/clients/ClientFile.tsx`**: Replaced the combined auth params list with a per-auth-scheme loop. Each auth scheme descriptor holds its param, doc, field assignment, and pipeline line. The first scheme gets short + full constructors; subsequent schemes get only the full constructor.
- **`test/scenarios/authentication/union_auth.md`**: Updated expected output to show separate constructors (ApiKey short + full, OAuth2 full only) instead of combined constructors.
- **`test/client-file.test.ts`**: Added new test `generates separate constructors per auth scheme for multi-auth clients` that verifies each constructor body is independent (no cross-contamination of auth fields/policies).

Pattern: `buildPipelineCreateLine` already handled individual auth schemes ŌĆö the fix was in how `RootClientConstructors` composes the constructors.

## 2026-03-04 ŌĆö Task 12.4: Verify ARM resource-manager specs generate correctly in e2e (DONE)

Ran `pnpm emit:e2e --filter azure/resource-manager` ŌĆö all 9 specs emit successfully (TypeSpecŌåÆC# generation works). However, none of the 9 specs compile with `dotnet build` due to missing emitter features for ARM-specific patterns.

**Error categories found:**
1. **AuthenticationTokenProvider not found (CS0246)** ŌĆö all 9 specs. The emitter generates `AuthenticationTokenProvider` references for OAuth2/bearer token auth but this type doesn't exist in System.ClientModel.
2. **Async paging methods with non-Task return types (CS1983)** ŌĆö 4 specs (method-subscription-id, operation-templates, resources). Methods marked `async` return `AsyncCollectionResult` directly instead of `Task<AsyncCollectionResult>`. The `async` keyword should be removed.
3. **Namespace/type name collision (CS0118)** ŌĆö method-subscription-id only. Sub-client classes (MixedSubscriptionPlacement, TwoSubscriptionResourcesMethodLevel) collide with their containing namespace names.
4. **Duplicate method overloads (CS0111)** ŌĆö resources only. Singleton generates both scalar and paging variants of `GetByResourceGroup` with identical parameter signatures but different return types.

**Actions taken:**
- Added all 9 ARM specs to `test/e2e/.testignore` with detailed comments per spec explaining each error
- Created 4 follow-up tasks in prd.json: 12.5 (AuthenticationTokenProvider), 12.6 (async paging), 12.7 (namespace collision), 12.8 (duplicate overloads)

**Patterns for next person:** The emit-e2e script's `--filter` flag is useful for testing specific spec categories. Use `dotnet build {csproj} --verbosity quiet 2>&1 | grep "error CS"` to quickly categorize compilation errors.

## 2026-03-04 ŌĆö Task 12.5: Fix AuthenticationTokenProvider namespace for OAuth2 auth (DONE)

### What was done
- Moved `AuthenticationTokenProvider` from `SystemClientModelPrimitives` (System.ClientModel.Primitives) to
  `SystemClientModel` (System.ClientModel) in `src/builtins/system-client-model.ts`. The actual .NET type
  lives in `System.ClientModel`, not `System.ClientModel.Primitives`.
- Removed unused `BearerTokenAuthenticationPolicy` from builtins (doesn't exist in System.ClientModel 1.9.0;
  the correct type is `BearerTokenPolicy` which was already defined).
- Updated `src/components/clients/ClientFile.tsx` to reference `SystemClientModel.AuthenticationTokenProvider`
  instead of `SystemClientModelPrimitives.AuthenticationTokenProvider`.
- Updated unit test comment and assertion in `test/client-file.test.ts` to verify `using System.ClientModel;`
  directive is generated for OAuth2 auth clients.
- Updated `test/e2e/.testignore` comments ŌĆö ARM specs now have model-level errors (CS0103/CS0191), NOT
  AuthenticationTokenProvider errors.

### Root cause
The Alloy `createLibrary()` namespace determines which `using` directive is auto-generated. Having
`AuthenticationTokenProvider` under `System.ClientModel.Primitives` caused Alloy to only generate
`using System.ClientModel.Primitives;`, but the real type needs `using System.ClientModel;`.

### Verification
- Re-emitted `azure/resource-manager/common-properties` spec ŌĆö confirmed CS0246 (AuthenticationTokenProvider)
  is gone. Remaining errors are CS0103 (Argument) and CS0191 (readonly field) from model serialization code.
- All 1,283 unit tests pass. No scenario test changes needed (they check class body, not using directives).

### Key learning
Always verify which .NET namespace a type belongs to before adding it to the Alloy builtins libraries.
Check the NuGet package XML docs: `grep "T:Full.Type.Name" ~/.nuget/packages/{pkg}/{ver}/lib/net8.0/{pkg}.xml`

## 2026-03-04 ŌĆö Task 12.6: Fix async keyword on paging methods returning AsyncCollectionResult (DONE)

**What**: Removed the `async` keyword from paging client methods that return `AsyncCollectionResult` or `AsyncCollectionResult<T>` in `PagingMethods.tsx`. These methods just instantiate and return a collection result object (no `await`), so `async` is incorrect and causes CS1983 errors.

- `test/scenarios/paging/server_driven_pagination.md` ŌĆö removed `async` from expected output

**Pattern**: Methods returning `AsyncCollectionResult`/`AsyncCollectionResult<T>` must NOT use `async` because they are not Task-based. The `async` keyword is only correct for methods returning `Task<T>` or `async IAsyncEnumerable<T>` (like the internal GetRawPagesAsync in CollectionResultFile.tsx which correctly uses it).

## 2026-03-04 ŌĆö Task 12.7: Fix namespace/type name collision for sub-client operation groups

**What was done:**
- Identified root cause: Alloy's C# naming policy applies `pascalCase()` to namespace segments,
  which strips the leading `_` prefix that `cleanAllNamespaces()` adds to prevent CS0118 errors
- Fixed `createHttpClientNamePolicy()` in `HttpClientCSharpOutput.tsx` to preserve underscore-
  prefixed namespace segments by short-circuiting the name policy when `element === "namespace"`
  and `name.startsWith("_")`
- Updated test expectations in `client-file.test.ts` for deeply nested sub-client test to
  expect underscore-prefixed namespace segments
- Added new test "escapes sub-client namespace segments that collide with class names"
- Updated `test/scenarios/enums/extensible_enum.md` via SCENARIOS_UPDATE=true to reflect
  correct `_Type._Enum.Extensible` namespace output (matches legacy emitter behavior)
- Verified fix against Azure ARM `method-subscription-id` spec: both `MixedSubscriptionPlacement`
  and `TwoSubscriptionResourcesMethodLevel` now correctly use `_`-prefixed namespaces

**Important for next iterations:**
- The fix is centralized in the name policy ŌĆö no per-component changes needed
- Scenario tests using TypeSpec namespaces with `Type`, `Enum`, `Array` segments now correctly
  generate underscore-prefixed C# namespaces matching the legacy emitter
- The `cleanAllNamespaces()` function was always working correctly; the bug was in rendering
- Other ARM specs in `.testignore` may now compile for the CS0118 issue (but other errors remain)

## 2026-03-04 ŌĆö Task 12.8: Fix duplicate method overloads for scalar vs paging operations with same name

**Problem:** In ARM Singleton resources, both `getByResourceGroup` (scalar) and `listByResourceGroup` (paging) exist. `cleanOperationName()` transforms `ListByResourceGroup` ŌåÆ `GetByResourceGroup`, colliding with the scalar method. C# CS0111 prevents overloads differing only in return type.

**Solution:** Extended `cleanOperationName()` with optional `siblingNames` parameter. When a ListŌåÆGet transformation would produce a name already present in the sibling set, the rename is skipped (method keeps its original PascalCase name). Created `buildSiblingNameSet()` helper to compute the sibling name set from `client.methods`.

**Files modified:**
- `src/utils/operation-naming.ts` ŌĆö added `siblingNames` param to `cleanOperationName`, added `buildSiblingNameSet` helper
- `src/components/clients/PagingMethods.tsx` ŌĆö compute & pass siblingNames
- `src/components/clients/ProtocolMethod.tsx` ŌĆö compute & pass siblingNames
- `src/components/clients/ConvenienceMethod.tsx` ŌĆö compute & pass siblingNames
- `src/components/clients/RestClientFile.tsx` ŌĆö compute & pass siblingNames to CreateRequestMethod
- `src/components/collection-results/CollectionResultFile.tsx` ŌĆö compute & pass siblingNames
- `test/operation-naming.test.ts` ŌĆö added collision avoidance tests
- `test/e2e/.testignore` ŌĆö removed CS0111 from resources spec comment

**Key pattern:** Sibling names are PascalCase names BEFORE cleaning, so pre-existing `GetXxx` names are visible as collision targets. The check is: if `cleanedName !== name && siblingNames.has(cleanedName)`, skip the rename.

**All 1,290 tests pass, build succeeds.**

## 2026-03-05 ŌĆö Task 12.10: Fix C# reserved keyword escaping in generated parameter names

**Problem:** TypeSpec specs with parameters named after C# reserved keywords (class, as, for, return, etc.) produce syntax errors (~1052) because parameter names lack the required `@` prefix.

**Root Cause:** The Alloy C# name policy only does case conversion (camelCase for params), not keyword escaping. The `escapeCSharpKeyword()` utility existed but was only used in CastOperators.tsx. Raw string interpolation sites in ProtocolMethod.tsx and ConvenienceMethod.tsx used `p.name` directly without escaping.

**Solution (two-pronged):**
1. Modified `createHttpClientNamePolicy()` in HttpClientCSharpOutput.tsx to call `escapeCSharpKeyword()` after the base policy's case conversion. This ensures `<Parameter>` declarations automatically render `@class` instead of `class`.
2. Applied `escapeCSharpKeyword()` at all raw C# string interpolation sites where parameter names appear outside JSX:
   - ProtocolMethod.tsx: argList (method call arguments), buildValidation
   - ConvenienceMethod.tsx: getProtocolCallArg, buildConvenienceValidation, buildSpreadProtocolCallExpr

**Files modified:**
- `src/components/HttpClientCSharpOutput.tsx` ŌĆö name policy now includes keyword escaping
- `src/components/clients/ProtocolMethod.tsx` ŌĆö imported escapeCSharpKeyword, fixed argList and buildValidation
- `src/components/clients/ConvenienceMethod.tsx` ŌĆö imported escapeCSharpKeyword, fixed getProtocolCallArg, buildConvenienceValidation, buildSpreadProtocolCallExpr
- `src/components/serialization/CastOperators.tsx` ŌĆö removed now-redundant explicit escapeCSharpKeyword call (name policy handles it)
- `test/protocol-method.test.ts` ŌĆö added keyword escaping test
- `test/convenience-method.test.ts` ŌĆö added keyword escaping test
- `test/csharp-keywords.test.ts` ŌĆö added idempotency test

**Design Decision:** Previous iteration (12.2.2) rejected the name policy approach due to concerns about "unexpected interactions with Alloy's internal name resolution." Analysis of Alloy's source code (OutputSymbol name setter, Name component, createParameterSymbol) showed no actual risk ŌĆö the `@` prefix is just part of the name string and doesn't affect symbol resolution. The name policy approach is strictly better because it automatically fixes all `<Parameter>` declarations, which can't be fixed by the call-site-only approach (camelCase strips `@` prefix).

**All 1,293 tests pass (3 new), build succeeds.**

## 2026-03-05 ŌĆö Task 12.9: Fix rootNamespace captured before cleanAllNamespaces

**What was done:** Fixed namespace mismatch where infrastructure files (Argument.cs, ClientUriBuilder.cs, etc.) used a stale pre-clean rootNamespace while client files used cleaned namespaces. Changed `const rootNamespace` to `let` and re-resolved after `cleanAllNamespaces()`.

**Files modified:**
- `src/emitter.tsx` ŌĆö changed `const` to `let`, added re-resolution after `cleanAllNamespaces()`
- `test/package-name.test.ts` ŌĆö added 2 tests validating rootNamespace reflects cleaned value

**Pattern:** `cleanAllNamespaces` mutates client objects by reference. `resolveRootNamespace` reads `sdkContext.sdkPackage.clients[0].namespace`. Since both share the same JS object references, re-calling `resolveRootNamespace` after cleaning returns the cleaned value.

**Note for next iteration:** The e2e test failure (dotnet test DLL path invalid) is pre-existing and unrelated to this change.

## 2026-03-05 ŌĆö Task 12.13: Fix namespace segment shadowing in generated code

**What was done:**
- Added `"File"` to `INVALID_NAMESPACE_SEGMENTS` in `src/utils/package-name.ts`
- This extends the existing static reserved words list (`Type`, `Array`, `Enum`) with `File`
- Updated JSDoc comment to explain why `File` is included
- Updated unit tests in `test/package-name.test.ts`:
  - Added `File` to reserved word detection test
  - Updated static reserved words count from 3 to 4
  - Added integration test for `_Type._File` namespace cleaning

**Root cause analysis:**
- The ORIGINAL issue described in task 12.13 (Type shadowing System.Type) was already fixed by task 12.9 (rootNamespace capture fix) + cleanAllNamespaces handling Type as a reserved word
- The REMAINING CS0118 errors (24 in type/file) were about `File` (a model type from TypeSpec.Http) being shadowed by the `File` namespace segment in `_Type.File._Body`
- C# name resolution rule: namespace segments in parent namespaces take precedence over imported type names

**Key decisions:**
- Added File to static list rather than dynamically detecting model-namespace conflicts, because:
  1. File is a common .NET type (System.IO.File) like Type, Array, Enum
  2. Dynamic detection would change currently-passing specs (Model, Query) unnecessarily
  3. The legacy emitter also doesn't handle model-namespace conflicts dynamically
- Only type/file spec was affected (verified no other specs use File as namespace segment)

**Patterns for next loops:**
- After this fix, type/file still has 16 CS0535 and CS1503 errors (unrelated: interface implementation + RequestOptions/CancellationToken conversion)
- The CS1503 errors are covered by task 12.14

2026-03-05 ŌĆö Task 12.11: Fix hyphenated HTTP header parameter names not converted to valid C# identifiers (complete)
- Root cause: buildConvenienceParams and buildProtocolParams stored raw TypeSpec parameter names (e.g., "x-ms-test-header") in param.name. While Alloy's <Method> component applies the naming policy for declarations, method bodies used raw names for validation, protocol call args, and XML docs.
- Fix: Added getParamName callback (namePolicy.getName(name, "parameter")) to both buildConvenienceParams and buildProtocolParams. All parameter names are now converted to valid camelCase C# identifiers (e.g., "xMsTestHeader") before being stored.
- Updated callers: ConvenienceMethods, ProtocolMethods, PagingMethods (renderProtocolPagingMethods, renderConveniencePagingMethods), CollectionResultFile.
- Added tests: convenience-method.test.ts and protocol-method.test.ts both have new tests validating hyphenated header names are converted in all usage sites.

## 2026-03-05 ŌĆö Task 12.14: Fix RequestOptions-to-CancellationToken argument conversion errors in convenience methods

**What was done:** Fixed CS1503 errors where convenience methods passed non-model body types directly to protocol methods, causing C# overload resolution to fail. The protocol method expects `(BinaryContent, RequestOptions)` but non-model types (enums, scalars, arrays, strings, BinaryData, internal spread models) lack implicit BinaryContent conversion, so C# would pick the convenience overload and error on the second arg.

**Root cause:** Only model types with `UsageFlags.Input` have `implicit operator BinaryContent`. All other body types passed as-is caused C# to resolve to the wrong overload.

**Fix:** Added `getBodyProtocolCallArg()` function that wraps non-model body types in `BinaryContentHelper.FromObject()` or `BinaryContentHelper.FromEnumerable()`:
- Model with Input flag ŌåÆ pass directly (implicit operator)
- Enum (string-backed) ŌåÆ `BinaryContentHelper.FromObject(body.ToString())`
- Enum (int-backed) ŌåÆ `BinaryContentHelper.FromObject((int)body)`
- Array ŌåÆ `BinaryContentHelper.FromEnumerable(body)`
- Other (string, BinaryData, scalar, dict, model without Input) ŌåÆ `BinaryContentHelper.FromObject(body)`

For spread bodies, modified `buildSpreadProtocolCallExpr()` to wrap the model constructor when the spread type lacks `UsageFlags.Input`: `BinaryContentHelper.FromObject(new SpreadModel(args))`.

**Files modified:**
- `src/components/clients/ConvenienceMethod.tsx` ŌĆö Added `getBodyProtocolCallArg`, `hasImplicitBinaryContentOperator`, updated `buildConvenienceParams` and `buildSpreadProtocolCallExpr`
- `test/convenience-method.test.ts` ŌĆö Added 4 tests: enum body wrapping, array body wrapping, string body wrapping, model body direct pass
- `test/scenarios/parameters/basic_implicit_body.md` ŌĆö Updated expected output for BinaryContentHelper wrapping
- `test/scenarios/parameters/spread_model.md` ŌĆö Updated spread model wrapping expectations
- `test/scenarios/payload/media_type_string_body.md` ŌĆö Updated string body wrapping expectations

**Result:** CS1503 RequestOptionsŌåÆCancellationToken errors reduced from 120 to 28. Remaining 24 are in `routes/` spec (IDictionary path params need string conversion ŌĆö different root cause) and 4 in `service/multi-service` (missing CancellationTokenExtensions ŌĆö different root cause).

**All 1,303 tests pass (7 new), build succeeds.**
